This contract (behavioral rules)\n\n**Human Role: Escalation Point (not observer)**\nHuman is not \"in the loop\" for normal flow, but IS the exception handler:\n- BLOCKED states with unresolvable questions → human resolves via `human_notes`\n- Kill switches (`PAUSE`, `ABORT`, `CHECKPOINT`) for system-wide intervention\n- Merge conflicts requiring judgment → human resolves in integration branch\n- Spec ambiguities that Orchestrator cannot resolve → human clarifies via `human_notes`\n\n---\n\n## Role Execution\n\nEach agent has a defined role with specific capabilities and constraints.\n\n| Role | Primary Function | Approval Authority |\n|------|------------------|-------------------|\n| **Orchestrator** | Decompose goals into tasks | None (creates work, doesn't approve) |\n| **Coder** | Implement tasks | None (submits for review) |\n| **Code Reviewer** | Review and merge | Approves/rejects Coder work |\n\n**Role Boundaries:**\n- Coders cannot self-approve\n- Coders cannot merge to integration branch\n- Code Reviewers cannot implement (only review and write new adversarial tests, not modify existing tests)\n- Orchestrators cannot claim implementation tasks\n\nViolating role boundaries is a Tier 1 violation — process integrity, not data/code integrity.\n\n---\n\n## Pre-Execution Checkpoint\n\nBefore implementation, write a checkpoint via `liza_write_checkpoint`:\nintent, assumptions, risks, validation plan, files to modify.\nSubmission is rejected without a checkpoint. The reviewer verifies\nimplementation matches checkpoint intent.\n\n---\n\n## Gate Semantics (Multi-Agent)\n\nThe Execution State Machine is defined in ~/.liza/CORE.md. In Multi-Agent mode:\n\n- **Gate artifact** = Pre-execution checkpoint written to blackboard (above)\n- **Gate cleared** = Checkpoint written (self-clearing — forces thinking, then proceed)\n\n## CORE Rule Overrides (Multi-Agent)\n\nThe following CORE.md rules have modified behavior in Multi-Agent Mode:\n\n| CORE Rule | Multi-Agent Behavior |\n|-----------|---------------------|\n| **Rule 1 Struggle Protocol** | Log anomaly → set BLOCKED |\n| **Rule 4 FAST PATH** | Reduced checkpoint: intent + files only |\n| **Debugging Protocol** | Do NOT debug autonomously beyond quick hypothesis. Log anomaly → BLOCKED. Rationale: autonomous debugging risks cascading errors across agents. |\n| **Context degradation** | Auto-checkpoint to blackboard, self-terminate |\n\n---\n\n## Blackboard Protocol\n\nThe blackboard (`state.yaml`) is the coordination mechanism.\n\n**Read Before Act:** Always read current state before any action.\n\n**History is Immutable:** Never delete history entries. Append only.\n\n**Do NOT edit state.yaml directly.** All state transitions MUST go through Liza MCP tools (`liza_submit_for_review`, `liza_claim_task`, etc.). Direct edits bypass invariant checks and can corrupt state irreversibly. If an MCP tool fails repeatedly, set the task BLOCKED via `liza_mark_blocked` — never work around the failure by editing state.yaml.\n\n**Do NOT use TodoWrite.** The blackboard already tracks task state and checkpoints.\n\n---\n\n## Iteration Protocol\n\nCoders iterate until approved or blocked.\n\nIteration and review cycle limits are enforced by the blackboard (see `config.max_coder_iterations`, `config.max_review_cycles`).\n\n**On Rejection:**\n1. Read rejection feedback from task\n2. Update checkpoint with new approach\n3. Implement fix\n4. Re-submit for review\n\n**Context Exhaustion Handoff (Coder only):**\nAt ~90% context (heuristic: many tool calls, re-reading files, difficulty holding state):\n1. STOP at next safe point\n2. Commit pending changes\n3. Use `liza_handoff` MCP tool with summary + next_action\n4. Exit with code 42\n\n**Review Exhaustion:**\nIf 2 different Code Reviewers fail to issue a verdict on the same task (exit without APPROVED/REJECTED):\n- Task is marked BLOCKED with `blocked_reason: \"review_exhaustion\"`\n- Orchestrator evaluates: spec unclear? done_when untestable?\n\n---\n\n## Scope Discipline (Liza-Specific)\n\n**Spec is Law:** Implementation must match spec exactly.\n- No \"improvements\" beyond spec\n- No \"obvious\" additions\n- No refactoring outside task scope\n\n**done_when is the Contract:**\nEach criterion is a test. All must pass. No more, no less.\nExample: `app greet` prints \"Hello, World!\", `app greet --name Alice` prints \"Hello, Alice!\"\n\n**TDD Enforcement:** Code tasks must include tests. Submission is rejected without test files\nunless the checkpoint declares `tdd_not_required` with justification (e.g. cosmetic-only change).\nThe reviewer verifies the justification.\n\n**scope Defines Boundaries:**\nIN-scope items specify what may be touched. Touching OUT-scope files is a violation.\n\n---\n\n## Context Recovery (Liza)\n\nWhen transitioning to Working Set tier (see CORE.md Context Management), re-read:\n\n**MAM-specific re-read list:**\n- Pre-Execution Checkpoint format (this file, \"Pre-Execution Checkpoint\")\n- Current role's constraints from your role section in the agent prompt\n- Active task from blackboard (re-read `state.yaml`)\n\nCombined with CORE.md universal items (Tier 0-1 rules, state machine, current task intent).\n\n---\n\n## Circuit Breaker\n\nAutomatic halt conditions:\n\n**Loop Detection Self-Abort:**\nIf an agent observes itself running:\n- The same command more than 3 times, OR\n- Close variations (same base, different flags/pipes) more than 5 times total\n\nWITHOUT meaningful progress → **STOP IMMEDIATELY**\n\n\"Meaningful progress\" = new information that changes next action. Piping same output through different tools is NOT progress.\n\n| Role | Log As | Then |\n|------|--------|------|\n| Coder | `retry_loop` | Mark task BLOCKED with diagnosis |\n| Code Reviewer | `reviewer_loop` | Issue REJECTED with `\"insufficient information to complete review\"` |\n| Orchestrator | `spec_gap` | Pause for human input |\n\nExit with code 42 after logging.\n\n---\n\nSecret word: MAS\n","numLines":185,"startLine":1,"totalLines":185}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01SqP9SSywYiFNyLx9q5Ai4i","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# OHM Website — Vision\n2\t\n3\t> **Purpose of this document:** This document expresses needs and constraints. It does not\n4\t> prescribe a technical stack. Stack proposals are to be derived from this vision by the\n5\t> architect, once the vision is stable.\n6\t\n7\tThe \"Orchestre d'Harmonie de Montrouge\" (OHM) is a French concert band, legally constituted as an association under the French law of 1901. This document describes the vision for its new website.\n8\t\n9\t## Current state\n10\t\n11\t### The current website\n12\t\n13\thttp://oh.montrouge.free.fr/\n14\t\n15\t- Built as static HTML, decades ago\n16\t- Hosted on Free.fr — storage quota exceeded, migration is required\n17\t- Sheet music is uploaded manually by one person\n18\t- All musicians share a single login and password, giving access to personal data\n19\t- Likely not GDPR compliant\n20\t- Visually outdated\n21\t\n22\t> **Open:** Source code location unknown.\n23\t\n24\t### OHM Agenda\n25\t\n26\tAn internal tool ([ohm-agenda](https://www.ohm-agenda.ovh/)) used to manage the association's activity:\n27\t\n28\t- Musicians subscribe to events\n29\t- Admins create events (concerts, rehearsals, other), manage musician records (name, instrument), and track annual fee payments per season\n30\t\n31\tSeason changes are manual: an admin must connect to [PhPMyAdmin](https://phpmyadmin.cluster021.hosting.ovh.net) and insert a row in the `season` table. The current season runs September–August; switching to January–December is under discussion and should be easy to support.\n32\t\n33\tThe database must not be lost. Migration is acceptable if the data model improves.\n34\t\n35\t- DB schema: `current/ohm-agenda/db_schema.sql`\n36\t- DB export (git-ignored): `current/ohm-agenda/db_export.sql`\n37\t\n38\t### Google Sheets\n39\t\n40\t[Drive folder](https://drive.google.com/drive/u/1/folders/1S5GoohHv_6DakVC0fzNoqGaLWUjp1nFB) — export available in the git-ignored folder `current/gdrive-liste-musiciens`\n41\t\n42\tA spreadsheet is maintained each season with musician information. It holds fields absent from OHM Agenda: phone number, address, job, birth date and place, nationality, and first inscription date. The schema is denormalized, making statistics unreliable and maintenance tedious. Fee payment is tracked here in parallel with OHM Agenda, duplicating work.\n43\t\n44\t## Problem\n45\t\n46\tOHM's operations depend on a handful of people, fragile tools, and a security model that cannot be defended.\n47\t\n48\tThe current website is maintained by a single person — if they leave, no one can update it. All musicians share one login and password to access a page that exposes personal data, creating both a security risk and a GDPR liability. Each season, admins must duplicate work across two tools, and creating a new season requires PhPMyAdmin access — a technical step most members cannot perform. Building statistics from a denormalized spreadsheet is painful, even though the underlying data could make it trivial.\n49\t\n50\tThe storage limit on the current host makes inaction impossible: staying would mean paying 10€/month to Free.fr for hosting already covered by OVH — money the association would rather spend on sheet music.\n51\t\n52\tThis project is primarily an **internal operations project**. The goal is to replace fragile, person-dependent processes with something any admin can run, that protects member data, and that consolidates the tools already in use into one place. A better public face is a secondary benefit.\n53\t\n54\t## Principles\n55\t\n56\t- **Keep it simple**: prefer the simplest solution that solves the problem.\n57\t- **Be lean**: defer decisions that have no present impact; do not design for hypothetical future needs.\n58\t\n59\t## Personas\n60\t\n61\t- **External users** — general public or potential new members\n62\t- **Musicians** — association members, regular performers\n63\t- **Admins** — association members with management privileges\n64\t\n65\t## Prerequisites\n66\t\n67\tThe following must be resolved before breaking this vision into epics and stories:\n68\t\n69\t1. **Stakeholder alignment** — OHM Agenda is a shared tool. All stakeholders must explicitly agree to migrate before V1 development begins. **Open.**\n70\t\n71\t2. **Data migration plan** — The Google Sheet contains fields absent from OHM Agenda (phone, address, job, birth date and place, nationality, first inscription date). Some may conflict with existing database records. A reconciliation plan will be defined during V1 implementation. The migration must import the complete fee payment history (covering all historical seasons) so that first inscription dates derived from the earliest recorded fee payment are accurate; first inscription date remains derived-only post-migration.\n72\t\n73\t3. **GDPR requirements** — Documented in [`specs/goals/gdpr.md`](gdpr.md). Reviewed.\n74\t\n75\t## Open Questions\n76\t\n77\t1. **OVH deployment target** — OVH offers several products (VPS, shared hosting, managed\n78\t   PaaS). The deployment target must be decided before technical specs can be written.\n79\t\n80\t## Milestones\n81\t\n82\t### V1 — Replace the old tools\n83\t\n84\t**Success condition:** OHM Agenda and the seasonal Google Sheet can be decommissioned, and Free.fr hosting can be abandoned.\n85\t\n86\t**Account model:** Admins create musician accounts. The system generates a one-time invite link, displayed in the UI for the admin to copy and send manually (e.g. from the association's email address); the musician follows it to a single-page form presenting: a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a combined phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form completes account setup and grants access. Password reset is also admin-mediated: the admin generates a one-time reset link in the UI, displayed for copying and sending manually. Invite links and password-reset links expire after 7 days. An expired invite link leaves the account in a pending state (cannot log in) — the admin can generate a new invite link at any time. An expired password-reset link leaves the account unaffected — the admin generates a new reset link. No system email infrastructure required.\n87\t\n88\tPhone and address share a single combined consent, given on the invite-link form. These fields are locked until consent is recorded; the admin can fill them only after consent is given. Birth date is optional. If provided and indicates the member is under 15, the parental consent URI field becomes required before the account can be saved. If birth date is left blank, no parental consent check is triggered. The system prevents removing the admin role from the last remaining admin account.\n89\t\n90\tAn account that has completed the invite flow is active. Account states: pending → active → anonymized (terminal). There is no separate deactivation — anonymization is the only mechanism for revoking login access.\n91\t\n92\tIn scope:\n93\t- Individual accounts — no more shared credentials; all accounts are musician accounts; the admin role is a permission that can be granted to any account\n94\t- Admin can grant or revoke the admin role on any account; the system prevents removing the admin role from the last remaining admin account\n95\t- Admin can create a season with a configurable date range and designate one as current — no more PhPMyAdmin; exactly one season is designated current at all times; the current designation cannot be removed without designating another season as current\n96\t- Admin can manage musicians; musician record fields: name, email, main instrument (from a controlled list sourced from OHM Agenda, plus \"Chef d'orchestre\"), birth date (optional; if provided and indicates under 15, a parental consent URI is required before the account can be saved), and phone/address (admin-editable only after the musician has given consent); parental consent URI, if set, is visible in the admin account detail view\n97\t- Admin can record a single fee payment per season for a musician, for any season (amount, date, type: chèque / espèces / virement bancaire; optional comment); payments can be edited or deleted; first inscription date is derived automatically from the musician's first recorded fee payment — no more Google Sheet duplication\n98\t- Admin can anonymize a musician account: all personal fields (name, email, birth date, phone, address, parental consent URI) are erased; main instrument is retained; fee payment records are anonymised (name replaced with a single opaque token generated at anonymization time and applied to all of that musician's payment records; season, amount, and payment type retained)\n99\t- Admin can delete a pending account (invite never accepted; no consent recorded)\n100\t- Admin can clear a musician's phone and address fields on the musician's behalf (consent withdrawal)\n101\t- Admin can create, edit, and delete events (name, date/time, type: concert / rehearsal / other — mirroring OHM Agenda); deleting an event removes all associated RSVP records (event deletion is the GDPR compliance path for RSVP records — RSVPs have a 2-year post-event retention; no separate cleanup tool in V1); new events start with all active accounts in an \"unanswered\" RSVP state; musicians can RSVP (yes / no / maybe) and change their RSVP at any time; all authenticated users can see the full RSVP list for an event (yes / no / maybe / unanswered; for concerts, the instrument of each musician who answered yes is also shown); when RSVPing yes to a concert, a musician selects which instrument they will play (main instrument pre-selected by default; changing a yes RSVP to no or maybe discards the selection); musicians who join after event creation start in the \"unanswered\" state for events that have not yet occurred — no more OHM Agenda\n102\t- Musician can view their own profile, showing: name, main instrument, email, birth date (if set), phone and address (if consented), and a static notice explaining how to withdraw consent for phone and address\n103\t- Musician can access sheet music via a single Google Drive link, configured at deploy time (no admin UI), displayed as a dedicated menu item to all authenticated users; the menu item is hidden if the link is not configured; access control is handled at the Google Drive level\n104\t- Admin can flag an account as \"processing restricted\" (GDPR Art. 18); has no operational effect in V1 beyond storage and display, and does not affect login\n105\t- Admin can view a list of accounts whose data retention period has elapsed\n106\t- Homepage: a public page presenting the association briefly, accessible to all visitors (authenticated and unauthenticated); It does not\n> prescribe a technical stack. Stack proposals are to be derived from this vision by the\n> architect, once the vision is stable.\n\nThe \"Orchestre d'Harmonie de Montrouge\" (OHM) is a French concert band, legally constituted as an association under the French law of 1901. This document describes the vision for its new website.\n\n## Current state\n\n### The current website\n\nhttp://oh.montrouge.free.fr/\n\n- Built as static HTML, decades ago\n- Hosted on Free.fr — storage quota exceeded, migration is required\n- Sheet music is uploaded manually by one person\n- All musicians share a single login and password, giving access to personal data\n- Likely not GDPR compliant\n- Visually outdated\n\n> **Open:** Source code location unknown.\n\n### OHM Agenda\n\nAn internal tool ([ohm-agenda](https://www.ohm-agenda.ovh/)) used to manage the association's activity:\n\n- Musicians subscribe to events\n- Admins create events (concerts, rehearsals, other), manage musician records (name, instrument), and track annual fee payments per season\n\nSeason changes are manual: an admin must connect to [PhPMyAdmin](https://phpmyadmin.cluster021.hosting.ovh.net) and insert a row in the `season` table. The current season runs September–August; switching to January–December is under discussion and should be easy to support.\n\nThe database must not be lost. Migration is acceptable if the data model improves.\n\n- DB schema: `current/ohm-agenda/db_schema.sql`\n- DB export (git-ignored): `current/ohm-agenda/db_export.sql`\n\n### Google Sheets\n\n[Drive folder](https://drive.google.com/drive/u/1/folders/1S5GoohHv_6DakVC0fzNoqGaLWUjp1nFB) — export available in the git-ignored folder `current/gdrive-liste-musiciens`\n\nA spreadsheet is maintained each season with musician information. It holds fields absent from OHM Agenda: phone number, address, job, birth date and place, nationality, and first inscription date. The schema is denormalized, making statistics unreliable and maintenance tedious. Fee payment is tracked here in parallel with OHM Agenda, duplicating work.\n\n## Problem\n\nOHM's operations depend on a handful of people, fragile tools, and a security model that cannot be defended.\n\nThe current website is maintained by a single person — if they leave, no one can update it. All musicians share one login and password to access a page that exposes personal data, creating both a security risk and a GDPR liability. Each season, admins must duplicate work across two tools, and creating a new season requires PhPMyAdmin access — a technical step most members cannot perform. Building statistics from a denormalized spreadsheet is painful, even though the underlying data could make it trivial.\n\nThe storage limit on the current host makes inaction impossible: staying would mean paying 10€/month to Free.fr for hosting already covered by OVH — money the association would rather spend on sheet music.\n\nThis project is primarily an **internal operations project**. The goal is to replace fragile, person-dependent processes with something any admin can run, that protects member data, and that consolidates the tools already in use into one place. A better public face is a secondary benefit.\n\n## Principles\n\n- **Keep it simple**: prefer the simplest solution that solves the problem.\n- **Be lean**: defer decisions that have no present impact; do not design for hypothetical future needs.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **External users** — general public or potential new members\n- **Musicians** — association members, regular performers\n- **Admins** — association members with management privileges\n\n## Prerequisites\n\nThe following must be resolved before breaking this vision into epics and stories:\n\n1. **Stakeholder alignment** — OHM Agenda is a shared tool. All stakeholders must explicitly agree to migrate before V1 development begins. **Open.**\n\n2. **Data migration plan** — The Google Sheet contains fields absent from OHM Agenda (phone, address, job, birth date and place, nationality, first inscription date). Some may conflict with existing database records. A reconciliation plan will be defined during V1 implementation. The migration must import the complete fee payment history (covering all historical seasons) so that first inscription dates derived from the earliest recorded fee payment are accurate; first inscription date remains derived-only post-migration.\n\n3. **GDPR requirements** — Documented in [`specs/goals/gdpr.md`](gdpr.md). Reviewed.\n\n## Open Questions\n\n1. **OVH deployment target** — OVH offers several products (VPS, shared hosting, managed\n   PaaS). The deployment target must be decided before technical specs can be written.\n\n## Milestones\n\n### V1 — Replace the old tools\n\n**Success condition:** OHM Agenda and the seasonal Google Sheet can be decommissioned, and Free.fr hosting can be abandoned.\n\n**Account model:** Admins create musician accounts. The system generates a one-time invite link, displayed in the UI for the admin to copy and send manually (e.g. from the association's email address); the musician follows it to a single-page form presenting: a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a combined phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form completes account setup and grants access. Password reset is also admin-mediated: the admin generates a one-time reset link in the UI, displayed for copying and sending manually. Invite links and password-reset links expire after 7 days. An expired invite link leaves the account in a pending state (cannot log in) — the admin can generate a new invite link at any time. An expired password-reset link leaves the account unaffected — the admin generates a new reset link. No system email infrastructure required.\n\nPhone and address share a single combined consent, given on the invite-link form. These fields are locked until consent is recorded; the admin can fill them only after consent is given. Birth date is optional. If provided and indicates the member is under 15, the parental consent URI field becomes required before the account can be saved. If birth date is left blank, no parental consent check is triggered. The system prevents removing the admin role from the last remaining admin account.\n\nAn account that has completed the invite flow is active. Account states: pending → active → anonymized (terminal). There is no separate deactivation — anonymization is the only mechanism for revoking login access.\n\nIn scope:\n- Individual accounts — no more shared credentials; all accounts are musician accounts; the admin role is a permission that can be granted to any account\n- Admin can grant or revoke the admin role on any account; the system prevents removing the admin role from the last remaining admin account\n- Admin can create a season with a configurable date range and designate one as current — no more PhPMyAdmin; exactly one season is designated current at all times; the current designation cannot be removed without designating another season as current\n- Admin can manage musicians; musician record fields: name, email, main instrument (from a controlled list sourced from OHM Agenda, plus \"Chef d'orchestre\"), birth date (optional; if provided and indicates under 15, a parental consent URI is required before the account can be saved), and phone/address (admin-editable only after the musician has given consent); parental consent URI, if set, is visible in the admin account detail view\n- Admin can record a single fee payment per season for a musician, for any season (amount, date, type: chèque / espèces / virement bancaire; optional comment); payments can be edited or deleted; first inscription date is derived automatically from the musician's first recorded fee payment — no more Google Sheet duplication\n- Admin can anonymize a musician account: all personal fields (name, email, birth date, phone, address, parental consent URI) are erased; main instrument is retained; fee payment records are anonymised (name replaced with a single opaque token generated at anonymization time and applied to all of that musician's payment records; season, amount, and payment type retained)\n- Admin can delete a pending account (invite never accepted; no consent recorded)\n- Admin can clear a musician's phone and address fields on the musician's behalf (consent withdrawal)\n- Admin can create, edit, and delete events (name, date/time, type: concert / rehearsal / other — mirroring OHM Agenda); deleting an event removes all associated RSVP records (event deletion is the GDPR compliance path for RSVP records — RSVPs have a 2-year post-event retention; no separate cleanup tool in V1); new events start with all active accounts in an \"unanswered\" RSVP state; musicians can RSVP (yes / no / maybe) and change their RSVP at any time; all authenticated users can see the full RSVP list for an event (yes / no / maybe / unanswered; for concerts, the instrument of each musician who answered yes is also shown); when RSVPing yes to a concert, a musician selects which instrument they will play (main instrument pre-selected by default; changing a yes RSVP to no or maybe discards the selection); musicians who join after event creation start in the \"unanswered\" state for events that have not yet occurred — no more OHM Agenda\n- Musician can view their own profile, showing: name, main instrument, email, birth date (if set), phone and address (if consented), and a static notice explaining how to withdraw consent for phone and address\n- Musician can access sheet music via a single Google Drive link, configured at deploy time (no admin UI), displayed as a dedicated menu item to all authenticated users; the menu item is hidden if the link is not configured; access control is handled at the Google Drive level\n- Admin can flag an account as \"processing restricted\" (GDPR Art. 18); has no operational effect in V1 beyond storage and display, and does not affect login\n- Admin can view a list of accounts whose data retention period has elapsed\n- Homepage: a public page presenting the association briefly, accessible to all visitors (authenticated and unauthenticated); content is static (bundled with the application)\n\nOut of scope:\n- Public-facing website and blog\n- Statistics page (data will be captured correctly; UI deferred)\n- Community manager role (decision deferred)\n\n#### Steps\n\n- [x] Iterate on the vision until a fresh-context prompt passes the gate:\n  > \"Review `specs/goals/vision.md` as a functional specification writer. In the next steps, you'll have to propose functional solutions — not technical ones. Apply KISS — default to the simplest reasonable interpretation — before flagging. Only flag items where the simplest interpretation is itself ambiguous or where two equally simple interpretations contradict each other.\"\n  - If you do any modification, ask the LLM to review the entire document for potentially introduced inconsistancies.\n- [x] Write functional specs in `specs/functional-specs/`\n  > \"You are a functional specificator. Your role is to propose functional solutions — not technical ones. Write functional\n    specs in `specs/functional-specs/`, applying KISS. When a genuinely blocking decision is encountered mid-writing, record\n    it as a functional ADR in `specs/functional-adrs/` before proceeding. Ensure the work is not lost if you reach usage limit.\"\n  - Gate: all blocking functional decisions recorded.\n- [x] Iterate on the functional specs until a fresh-context prompt passes the gate:\n  > \"Review `specs/goals/vision.md` and `specs/functional-specs/` as a technical specification writer. In the next steps, you'll have to propose technical solutions. Apply KISS — default to the simplest reasonable interpretation — before flagging. Only flag items where the simplest interpretation is itself ambiguous or where two equally simple interpretations contradict each other.\"\n- [ ] Write technical specs in `specs/technical-specs/`\n  > \"You are a technical specificator. Your role is to propose technical solutions. Write technical\n    specs in `specs/technical-specs/`, applying KISS. When a genuinely blocking decision is encountered mid-writing, record\n    it as a technical ADR in `specs/technical-adrs/` before proceeding. The admin can generate a fresh invite token.\n53\t\n54\t---\n55\t\n56\t## Password Reset\n57\t\n58\t1. The PasswordResetToken expires 7 days after generation. If it expires unused, the account is\n61\t   unaffected. The admin can generate a new reset token at any time; doing so invalidates any\n62\t   existing token for that account.\n63\t3. The musician follows the reset URL and is presented with a new password field.\n64\t4. The musician submits the new password. The account remains `active` with the updated\n65\t   password. The PasswordResetToken is marked used.\n66\t\n67\t**Expired or already-used reset URL:** The system displays an informative message. The account\n68\tis unaffected. The admin generates a new reset token.\n69\t\n70\tPassword reset is not available for `pending` or `anonymized` accounts.\n71\t\n72\t---\n73\t\n74\t## Last-Admin Protection\n75\t\n76\tThe system must always have at least one `active` account with the admin flag set.\n77\t\n78\tThe following operations are blocked if they would result in zero active admin accounts:\n79\t- Removing the admin flag from an account\n80\t- Anonymizing an admin account\n81\t- Deleting a pending admin account\n82\t\n83\tIn each case, the system rejects the operation with an informative message.\n84\t\n85\t---\n86\t\n87\t## Sheet Music Access\n88\t\n89\tWhen a Google Drive link is configured at deploy time, a \"Partitions\" menu item is shown to all\n90\tauthenticated (logged-in) users. Admin creates a musician account (see [Musician Management](02-musician-management.md)).\n   The account is created in `pending` state.\n2. On creation, the system generates an InviteToken. The corresponding invite URL is displayed\n   in the admin UI for the admin to copy and send manually (e.g., from the association's email\n   address).\n3. After the invite flow, the musician lands on their home page.\n\n**Expired or already-used invite URL:** The system displays an informative message. The account\nremains `pending`. The admin can generate a fresh invite token.\n\n---\n\n## Password Reset\n\n1. The PasswordResetToken expires 7 days after generation. If it expires unused, the account is\n   unaffected. The admin can generate a new reset token at any time; doing so invalidates any\n   existing token for that account.\n3. The musician follows the reset URL and is presented with a new password field.\n4. The musician submits the new password. The account remains `active` with the updated\n   password. The PasswordResetToken is marked used.\n\n**Expired or already-used reset URL:** The system displays an informative message. The account\nis unaffected. The item opens the configured Drive URL. If no link is\nconfigured, the menu item is hidden.\n\nThere is no admin UI to manage this link; it is set at application configuration time.\n","numLines":94,"startLine":1,"totalLines":94}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01YbQKpyejyA3i4d2PwBFCxj","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# OHM Website — Authentication and Security\n2\t\n3\t> **Depends on:** [Functional Account Lifecycle](../functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md)\n4\t> **ADRs:** [001 — Authentication: Server-Side Sessions](../technical-adrs/001-authentication.md),\n5\t> [004 — Framework and Language](../technical-adrs/004-framework-and-language.md)\n6\t\n7\t---\n8\t\n9\t## Session-Based Authentication\n10\t\n11\tAuthentication uses server-side sessions per ADR 001.\n12\t\n13\t- On successful login, a session record is created server-side and a session ID is set in a\n14\t  cookie.\n15\t- **Cookie flags:** HttpOnly (no JS access), Secure (HTTPS only), SameSite=Strict.\n16\t- Only `active` accounts may log in. The application checks account status before creating a\n17\t  session.\n18\t- On anonymization, the account's session (if any) is invalidated server-side. The cookie\n19\t  becomes stale and subsequent requests are treated as unauthenticated.\n20\t- Session lifetime: 7 days rolling, via `MaxAge` on the `pgstore` session store.\n21\t- Session store: `pgstore` — a PostgreSQL-backed `gorilla/sessions` store. Sessions are kept in\n22\t  a `sessions` table managed by pgstore. Required for ADR 001: the session row is deleted on\n23\t  account anonymization, immediately revoking access regardless of cookie expiry.\n24\t\n25\t---\n26\t\n27\t## Password Hashing\n28\t\n29\tPasswords are hashed with **Argon2id**.\n30\t\n31\t- Parameters: use the library's recommended defaults unless performance tuning is required.\n32\t  Minimum: time cost ≥ 1, memory cost ≥ 64 MiB, parallelism ≥ 1.\n33\t- Passwords are never stored in plain text or logged.\n34\t- Passwords are never retrievable; only verification is supported.\n35\t- On account anonymization, the stored password hash is cleared (set to null).\n36\t\n37\t---\n38\t\n39\t## Token Generation\n40\t\n41\tAll application tokens (InviteToken, PasswordResetToken, anonymization token) are generated as:\n42\t- **Source:** CSPRNG (cryptographically secure random number generator)\n43\t- **Length:** 32 random bytes\n44\t- **Encoding:** base64url (URL-safe, no padding)\n45\t\n46\tThe anonymization token must not be derived from the account ID or any other stable identifier.\n47\t\n48\t---\n49\t\n50\t## CSRF Protection\n51\t\n52\tAll state-changing requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) are protected via `gorilla/csrf`,\n53\tintegrated in the Buffalo middleware stack. Plush templates expose the token via\n54\t`<%= authenticity_token %>` (Buffalo convention). Requests missing a valid token are rejected\n55\twith HTTP 403.\n56\t\n57\tCombined with SameSite=Strict on the session cookie, this provides defense in depth.\n58\t\n59\t---\n60\t\n61\t## Public Routes\n62\t\n63\tThe following routes are accessible without authentication:\n64\t\n65\t| Route | Purpose |\n66\t|-------|---------|\n67\t| `/politique-de-confidentialite` | Privacy notice (static page) |\n68\t| `/invite/:token` | Invite flow (account setup) |\n69\t| `/reinitialiser-mot-de-passe/:token` | Password reset |\n70\t\n71\tAll other routes require an active-account session. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes\n72\tare redirected to the login page.\n73\t\n74\tThe login page itself is public (no redirect loop).\n75\t\n76\t---\n77\t\n78\t## Role Checks\n79\t\n80\tTwo access levels exist:\n81\t\n82\t| Level | Condition |\n83\t|-------|-----------|\n84\t| Authenticated | Session exists for an `active` account |\n85\t| Admin | Authenticated + a row exists in `account_roles` joining to `roles.name = 'admin'` for this account |\n86\t\n87\tAdmin-only routes and operations must verify both conditions. The check must be re-evaluated on\n88\teach request by querying `account_roles`; a cached claim from session creation is not sufficient\n89\t(roles can be revoked while a session is active). See ADR 005.\n90\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4affd881-5ee2-42ba-96d1-34f2389069cd","uuid":"454e647e-3a3e-4927-844d-13d2ec6d8881","timestamp":"2026-04-12T14:38:45.272Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/henry/workspace/ohm-website/specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md","content":"# OHM Website — Authentication and Security\n\n> **Depends on:** [Functional Account Lifecycle](../functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md)\n> **ADRs:** [001 — Authentication: Server-Side Sessions](../technical-adrs/001-authentication.md),\n> [004 — Framework and Language](../technical-adrs/004-framework-and-language.md)\n\n---\n\n## Session-Based Authentication\n\nAuthentication uses server-side sessions per ADR 001.\n\n- On successful login, a session record is created server-side and a session ID is set in a\n  cookie.\n- **Cookie flags:** HttpOnly (no JS access), Secure (HTTPS only), SameSite=Strict.\n- Only `active` accounts may log in. The application checks account status before creating a\n  session.\n- On anonymization, the account's session (if any) is invalidated server-side. The cookie\n  becomes stale and subsequent requests are treated as unauthenticated.\n- Session lifetime: 7 days rolling, via `MaxAge` on the `pgstore` session store.\n- Session store: `pgstore` — a PostgreSQL-backed `gorilla/sessions` store. Sessions are kept in\n  a `sessions` table managed by pgstore. Required for ADR 001: the session row is deleted on\n  account anonymization, immediately revoking access regardless of cookie expiry.\n\n---\n\n## Password Hashing\n\nPasswords are hashed with **Argon2id**.\n\n- Parameters: use the library's recommended defaults unless performance tuning is required.\n  Minimum: time cost ≥ 1, memory cost ≥ 64 MiB, parallelism ≥ 1.\n- Passwords are never stored in plain text or logged.\n- Passwords are never retrievable; only verification is supported.\n- On account anonymization, the stored password hash is cleared (set to null).\n\n---\n\n## Token Generation\n\nAll application tokens (InviteToken, PasswordResetToken, anonymization token) are generated as:\n- **Source:** CSPRNG (cryptographically secure random number generator)\n- **Length:** 32 random bytes\n- **Encoding:** base64url (URL-safe, no padding)\n\nThe anonymization token must not be derived from the account ID or any other stable identifier.\n\n---\n\n## CSRF Protection\n\nAll state-changing requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) are protected via `gorilla/csrf`,\nintegrated in the Buffalo middleware stack. Plush templates expose the token via\n`<%= authenticity_token %>` (Buffalo convention). Requests missing a valid token are rejected\nwith HTTP 403.\n\nCombined with SameSite=Strict on the session cookie, this provides defense in depth.\n\n---\n\n## Public Routes\n\nThe following routes are accessible without authentication:\n\n| Route | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `/politique-de-confidentialite` | Privacy notice (static page) |\n| `/invite/:token` | Invite flow (account setup) |\n| `/reinitialiser-mot-de-passe/:token` | Password reset |\n\nAll other routes require an active-account session. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes\nare redirected to the login page.\n\nThe login page itself is public (no redirect loop).\n\n---\n\n## Role Checks\n\nTwo access levels exist:\n\n| Level | Condition |\n|-------|-----------|\n| Authenticated | Session exists for an `active` account |\n| Admin | Authenticated + a row exists in `account_roles` joining to `roles.name = 'admin'` for this account |\n\nAdmin-only routes and operations must verify both conditions. The check must be re-evaluated on\neach request by querying `account_roles`; a cached claim from session creation is not sufficient\n(roles can be revoked while a session is active). See ADR 005.\n","numLines":90,"startLine":1,"totalLines":90}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CVSLJM41tidJE3s6gicNB6","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR 001 — Authentication: Server-Side Sessions\n2\t\n3\t| Field | Value |\n4\t|-------|-------|\n5\t| Status | Accepted |\n6\t| Date | 2026-04-11 |\n7\t\n8\t## Context\n9\t\n10\tThe application requires authentication: only `active` accounts may access protected routes. Two\n11\tmain approaches exist:\n12\t\n13\t1. **Server-side sessions** — a session record is stored server-side; the client holds an opaque\n14\t   session ID in a cookie.\n15\t2. **Stateless tokens (JWT / PASETO)** — the client holds a signed token containing the session\n16\t   claims; the server verifies the signature on each request without a session store.\n17\t\n18\tA constraint from the functional spec: when an account is anonymized, its login access must be\n19\trevoked immediately.\n20\t\n21\t## Decision\n22\t\n23\t**Server-side sessions with an HttpOnly + Secure + SameSite=Strict cookie.**\n24\t\n25\t## Rationale\n26\t\n27\t1. **Immediate revocation.** Anonymization must revoke login access on the spot. With server-side\n28\t   sessions, invalidating the session record is sufficient. With stateless tokens, a revocation\n29\t   list is required — equivalent complexity to a session store, with none of the simplicity\n30\t   benefit.\n31\t\n32\t2. **No public API in V1.** Stateless tokens' main advantage is enabling stateless horizontal\n33\t   scaling and cross-origin API access. V1 has neither: the client is the server-rendered\n34\t   application, and there is no public API surface.\n35\t\n36\t3. **Simpler implementation.** No key management, no token expiry/refresh logic, no clock-skew\n37\t   considerations.\n38\t\n39\t## Consequences\n40\t\n41\t- A session store is required. For a single-server OVH deployment, a DB-backed session store\n42\t  (same DB as the application) is sufficient. An in-memory store is acceptable for local\n43\t  development only.\n44\t- Session lifetime and expiry policy (rolling vs. absolute) are defined in the technical specs.\n45\t- Cookie flags: HttpOnly (no JS access), Secure (HTTPS only), SameSite=Strict (CSRF\n46\t  mitigation layer 1).\n47\t\n48\t## Alternatives Considered\n49\t\n50\t**JWT / PASETO:** Rejected. Adds key management and token refresh complexity. Immediate\n51\trevocation requires a revocation list, eliminating the stateless advantage. No V1 use case\n52\tjustifies the trade-off.\n53\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4affd881-5ee2-42ba-96d1-34f2389069cd","uuid":"f51eec9a-9299-4f6b-a2c7-1e722d5c187d","timestamp":"2026-04-12T14:38:45.627Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/henry/workspace/ohm-website/specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md","content":"# ADR 001 — Authentication: Server-Side Sessions\n\n| Field | Value |\n|-------|-------|\n| Status | Accepted |\n| Date | 2026-04-11 |\n\n## Context\n\nThe application requires authentication: only `active` accounts may access protected routes. Two\nmain approaches exist:\n\n1. **Server-side sessions** — a session record is stored server-side; the client holds an opaque\n   session ID in a cookie.\n2. **Stateless tokens (JWT / PASETO)** — the client holds a signed token containing the session\n   claims; the server verifies the signature on each request without a session store.\n\nA constraint from the functional spec: when an account is anonymized, its login access must be\nrevoked immediately.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Server-side sessions with an HttpOnly + Secure + SameSite=Strict cookie.**\n\n## Rationale\n\n1. **Immediate revocation.** Anonymization must revoke login access on the spot. With server-side\n   sessions, invalidating the session record is sufficient. With stateless tokens, a revocation\n   list is required — equivalent complexity to a session store, with none of the simplicity\n   benefit.\n\n2. **No public API in V1.** Stateless tokens' main advantage is enabling stateless horizontal\n   scaling and cross-origin API access. V1 has neither: the client is the server-rendered\n   application, and there is no public API surface.\n\n3. **Simpler implementation.** No key management, no token expiry/refresh logic, no clock-skew\n   considerations.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- A session store is required. For a single-server OVH deployment, a DB-backed session store\n  (same DB as the application) is sufficient. An in-memory store is acceptable for local\n  development only.\n- Session lifetime and expiry policy (rolling vs. absolute) are defined in the technical specs.\n- Cookie flags: HttpOnly (no JS access), Secure (HTTPS only), SameSite=Strict (CSRF\n  mitigation layer 1).\n\n## Alternatives Considered\n\n**JWT / PASETO:** Rejected. Adds key management and token refresh complexity. Immediate\nrevocation requires a revocation list, eliminating the stateless advantage. No V1 use case\njustifies the trade-off.\n","numLines":53,"startLine":1,"totalLines":53}}}

Migrations are written in Fizz DSL (Pop's\n> migration format); see [`03-stack.md`](03-stack.md). Exact DDL lives in `migrations/`.\n\n---\n\n## accounts\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| first_name | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized |\n| last_name | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized |\n| email | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized. See uniqueness constraint below. |\n| password_hash | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized. Argon2id. |\n| main_instrument_id | BIGINT FK → instruments | No | Retained on anonymization |\n| birth_date | DATE | Yes | Null when anonymized or not provided |\n| parental_consent_uri | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized or not applicable |\n| phone | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized, consent withdrawn, or not provided |\n| address | TEXT | Yes | Null when anonymized, consent withdrawn, or not provided |\n| phone_address_consent | BOOLEAN | No | Default false. False when anonymized or withdrawn. |\n| status | TEXT | No | `pending` \\| `active` \\| `anonymized` |\n| processing_restricted | BOOLEAN | No | Default false. False when anonymized. |\n| anonymization_token | TEXT | Yes | Set at anonymization time. Null otherwise. |\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Partial unique index on `email WHERE status != 'anonymized'`. Multiple anonymized rows may\n  have null email; this does not conflict with the uniqueness constraint.\n- Application invariant (not DB-enforced): at all times, at least one `active` account holds\n  the `admin` role. Enforced by last-admin protection checks before any operation that could\n  reduce this count to zero. See ADR 005.\n\n---\n\n## roles\n\nA controlled list of permission roles. Seeded by migration; no admin UI in V1.\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| name | TEXT UNIQUE | No | e.g. `admin` |\n\nSeeded with a single entry: `admin`. See ADR 005.\n\n---\n\n## account_roles\n\nAssociation table granting a role to an account.\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| account_id | BIGINT FK → accounts | No | ON DELETE CASCADE |\n| role_id | BIGINT FK → roles | No | — |\n\n**Constraint:** `PRIMARY KEY (account_id, role_id)` — one assignment per (account, role) pair.\n\n`ON DELETE CASCADE` on `account_id` covers hard deletion of `pending` accounts. For\nanonymization (account row is retained), roles are removed explicitly:\n`DELETE FROM account_roles WHERE account_id = $1`.\n\n---\n\n## instruments\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| name | TEXT UNIQUE | No | — |\n\nPopulated by seed/migration data (OHM Agenda instrument list + \"Chef d'orchestre\"). No admin UI\nto add or remove instruments in V1.\n\n---\n\n## seasons\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| label | TEXT | No | e.g. \"2025-2026\" |\n| start_date | DATE | No | — |\n| end_date | DATE | No | — |\n| is_current | BOOLEAN | No | Default false |\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Partial unique index on `is_current WHERE is_current = true`. Ensures at most one season is\n  designated current at the DB level.\n- Application invariant: exactly one season has `is_current = true` once any season has been\n  designated current. The invariant does not apply in the empty state (before any season is\n  created). Designation transfers are executed in a single transaction.\n- Seasons are immutable after creation (label, start_date, end_date). Enforced by the\n  application; no DB trigger required.\n\n---\n\n## fee_payments\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| account_id | BIGINT FK → accounts | No | FK is retained after account anonymization. The anonymization token is read from the account record. |\n| season_id | BIGINT FK → seasons | No | — |\n| amount | NUMERIC(10, 2) | No | — |\n| payment_date | DATE | No | The date the payment was made |\n| payment_type | TEXT | No | `chèque` \\| `espèces` \\| `virement bancaire` |\n| comment | TEXT | Yes | — |\n\n**Constraints:**\n- `UNIQUE(account_id, season_id)` — at most one payment per account per season.\n\n**On anonymization:** The FK `account_id` continues to reference the now-anonymized account\nrecord. Display logic reads `accounts.anonymization_token` in place of the account name. No\ncolumn in `fee_payments` changes at anonymization time.\n\n---\n\n## events\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| name | TEXT | No | — |\n| datetime | TIMESTAMPTZ | No | Stored as UTC. See ADR 002. |\n| event_type | TEXT | No | `concert` \\| `rehearsal` \\| `other` |\n\n---\n\n## rsvps\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| account_id | BIGINT FK → accounts | No | — |\n| event_id | BIGINT FK → events | No | Cascade delete when event is deleted |\n| state | TEXT | No | `unanswered` \\| `yes` \\| `no` \\| `maybe` |\n| instrument_id | BIGINT FK → instruments | Yes | Non-null only when state = `yes` and event type = `concert` |\n\n**Constraints:**\n- `UNIQUE(account_id, event_id)` — DB-level guard against duplicate RSVPs (e.g. from concurrent\n  event creation and account activation).\n- Cascade delete on `event_id`: deleting an event removes all its RSVP records.\n\n---\n\n## event_fields\n\nCustom fields defined by an admin on `other`-type events.\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| event_id | BIGINT FK → events | No | Cascade delete when event is deleted |\n| label | TEXT | No | — |\n| field_type | TEXT | No | `choice` \\| `integer` \\| `text` |\n| required | BOOLEAN | No | Default false |\n| position | INTEGER | No | Display order |\n\n---\n\n## event_field_choices\n\nSelectable options for `choice`-type event fields.\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| event_field_id | BIGINT FK → event_fields | No | Cascade delete when field is deleted |\n| label | TEXT | No | — |\n| position | INTEGER | No | Display order |\n\n---\n\n## rsvp_field_responses\n\nA musician's response to a single event field, captured as part of a `yes` RSVP.\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| rsvp_id | BIGINT FK → rsvps | No | Cascade delete when RSVP is deleted |\n| event_field_id | BIGINT FK → event_fields | No | Cascade delete when field is deleted |\n| value | TEXT | No | Stored as text regardless of field type |\n\n**Constraint:** `UNIQUE(rsvp_id, event_field_id)` — one response per (RSVP, field) pair.\n\n---\n\n## invite_tokens\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| account_id | BIGINT FK → accounts | No | — |\n| token | TEXT UNIQUE | No | CSPRNG, 32 bytes, base64url-encoded |\n| expires_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | No | UTC. 7 days from generation. |\n| used | BOOLEAN | No | Default false. Set true when invite flow completes. |\n\nAt most one active (unused, non-expired) token per account. Generating a new token marks any\nexisting token for that account as used.\n\n---\n\n## password_reset_tokens\n\n| Column | Type | Nullable | Notes |\n|--------|------|----------|-------|\n| id | BIGSERIAL PK | No | — |\n| account_id | BIGINT FK → accounts | No | — |\n| token | TEXT UNIQUE | No | CSPRNG, 32 bytes, base64url-encoded |\n| expires_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | No | UTC. 7 days from generation. |\n| used | BOOLEAN | No | Default false. Set true when password is changed. |\n\nAt most one active (unused, non-expired) token per account. This\n87\tinvariant applies in steady state (once any season has been created and designated current).\n88\t\n89\tBefore the first season is created, the system has no current season. This is an acceptable\n90\ttransient state during initial setup. The application does not enforce the invariant on an empty\n91\t`seasons` table; it enforces it on any operation that would remove the current designation from\n92\tan existing season (transferring it to another).\n93\t\n94\t**Recommended setup sequence after first deployment:**\n95\t1. See [CI/CD spec](06-ci-cd.md).\n\n**Usage context:** One-time setup after first deployment. Not exposed as an HTTP endpoint.\n\n---\n\n## Emergency Admin Recovery\n\nFor use when the last admin cannot log in (forgotten password, corrupted credential). Bypasses\nthe normal password reset flow, which requires an admin to already be logged in.\n\n**Behaviour:**\n- Accepts an email address and a new password as arguments (or interactive prompt).\n- Verifies the account exists with `status = 'active'`.\n- Generates a new Argon2id hash and writes it directly to `accounts.password_hash`.\n- Does not check for admin role — this is intentional (it is a recovery tool, not a\n  management operation).\n- The password is hashed before storage; it is never echoed or logged.\n\n**Implementation:** Grift task in `grifts/db.go`, invoked via `mise run recover-admin`\n(wraps `buffalo task db:recover:admin`).\n\n**Usage context:** Emergency recovery only. Never exposed as an HTTP endpoint.\n\n---\n\n## Development Seed Data\n\nA separate grift task populates the local database with realistic dummy data for development:\nseveral musicians in varied states (pending, active), a current season, past seasons, events\nof each type with RSVPs, and fee payment records.\n\n**Implementation:** `grifts/db.go`, invoked via `mise run seed-dev` (wraps\n`buffalo task db:seed:dev`).\n\n**Usage context:** Local development only. Never run against production.\n\n---\n\n## Instrument Seed Data\n\nThe instrument list is fixed at migration time. A seed migration populates the `instruments`\ntable from the OHM Agenda controlled list, plus \"Chef d'orchestre\". No admin UI exists to add\nor remove instruments in V1.\n\nThe list is extracted from OHM Agenda at migration time (`current/ohm-agenda/db_schema.sql`\nor `db_export.sql`). \"Chef d'orchestre\" is not present in the OHM Agenda export; the migration\nadds it explicitly as an additional row.\n\n---\n\n## Season Invariant and Initial State\n\nThe functional spec requires exactly one season to be designated current at all times. This\ninvariant applies in steady state (once any season has been created and designated current).\n\nBefore the first season is created, the system has no current season. This is an acceptable\ntransient state during initial setup. The application does not enforce the invariant on an empty\n`seasons` table; it enforces it on any operation that would remove the current designation from\nan existing season (transferring it to another).\n\n**Recommended setup sequence after first deployment:**\n1. Run the bootstrap CLI to create the first admin account.\n2. Log in and create the initial season.\n3. Designate the initial season as current.\n\nNo seed season is created by migrations; real seasons are created by the admin.\n\n---\n\n## Schema Versioning\n\nDB schema changes are managed through Pop migrations (Fizz DSL or raw SQL), located in\n`migrations/`. Each migration file has an `up` and `down` direction.\n\n**Commands:**\n- `buffalo pop migrate` — apply all pending migrations\n- `buffalo pop migrate --rollback` — roll back the last applied migration\n- `buffalo pop migrate status` — list applied and pending migrations\n\nConventions:\n- One migration file per logical schema change.\n- Migration files are named with a timestamp prefix (generated by `buffalo pop g model`).\n- Migrations are applied in order and never modified after deployment.\n- Pop tracks applied migrations in a `schema_migration` table.\n","numLines":118,"startLine":1,"totalLines":118}}}

Let me evaluate these against the persona clusters to see which decomposition actually maps to how different users interact with the system. I'm re-reading the task description and noticing it explicitly calls out two groupings: core authentication (invite links, password reset, login/logout, session management) and account lifecycle (user states, admin roles, last-admin protection, sheet music access). This aligns better with what the task owner is looking for, so I'll restructure around EP-001 for Core Authentication Flows and EP-002 for Account Lifecycle and Privileges. Now I'm mapping out the capabilities within each epic, starting with the authentication flows.\n\nFor CAP-001 covering the invite flow, I'm counting six stories: admin generates and displays the invite link, admin can regenerate it to invalidate the old one, musician opens the link and sees the setup form, musician completes setup to activate the account, and handling expired or used links. That gives me a solid 6 stories, which fits the 3-8 range. Now I'm working through CAP-002 for login and session management to see if it also lands in that range. I'm realizing the account state model is more foundational than a user-facing capability—the actual transitions happen elsewhere (pending→active in the invite flow, active→anonymized in EP-004). For EP-002, I should focus on the concrete admin capabilities: role grant/revoke with its UI, last-admin protection as a cross-cutting constraint, and pending account deletion.\n\nBreaking down CAP-001 (Admin role), I have four distinct stories covering granting and revoking roles, checking admin status on every request, and returning 403 for non-admins. CAP-002 (Last-admin protection) gives me three stories—blocking revocation, anonymization, and deletion of the last admin—but that might be too thin as its own capability. I'm considering whether to merge it with CAP-001 since last-admin protection is really a constraint that applies across multiple operations rather than a standalone feature.\n\nIf I combine them into a single capability around admin role management, I get five stories total: granting admin access, revoking it, preventing revocation of the last admin, verifying the role on every request, and enforcing 403 responses for unauthorized access. That feels like a solid grouping.\n\nFor CAP-002 (Sheet music access), I'm looking at three stories around the \"Partitions\" menu—showing it when configured, hiding it when not, and opening the Google Drive link. It's a small capability, but I'm wondering if it stands on its own or if it should be bundled with something else.\n\nStepping back, I'm evaluating whether EP-001 and EP-002 are structured well. EP-001 covers core auth flows across three capabilities with roughly 18 stories, while EP-002 handles admin roles and sheet music with about 8 stories. EP-001 feels a bit heavy, but breaking it down further might fragment the work too much. From a Story Writer perspective, each capability becomes a self-contained task brief, so the current structure should work fine.\n\nLooking at the actual story distribution across all five capabilities—invite flow, login/session, password reset, admin roles with last-admin protection, and sheet music—I'm getting 26 stories total. That's substantial for Phase 1, but authentication is genuinely complex work, so it tracks.\n\nThe epic-writing guidance is clear: each capability should decompose into 3–8 user stories and become its own Story Writer task. Since the instructions encourage producing multiple well-focused epics from a single vision, I'm splitting this into two epics instead of cramming everything into one. EP-001 covers the core authentication flows (invitation, login/session, password reset), while EP-002 handles the privilege layer (admin roles and sheet music {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /home/henry/.claude/skills/epic-writing\n\n# Objective\n\nTransform a vision document or high-level product requirement into a structured epic — a markdown\ndocument, git-tracked, treated with the same rigor as code.\n\nAn epic is the primary input to the **user-story-writing** skill. Each capability section becomes a\nStory Writer task: the Story Writer reads the epic's Personas, General Information, and the\ncapability section — nothing else. Write accordingly. A capability that requires the Story Writer\nto re-read the vision to understand what they're building is incomplete.\n\nAn epic bounds one cohesive capability area, serving a coherent persona cluster, expected to\ndecompose into **3–8 user stories** across its capabilities. It lives one level above user stories.\nIts job is to answer: *what is being built, for whom, and what is explicitly out of scope* — not\nhow. It decomposes into capabilities; capabilities decompose into story documents.\n\n# Trigger\n\nUse this skill when:\n- Orchestrator creates an epic-writing task (Liza mode)\n- User asks to write an epic for a feature area or product milestone (Pairing mode)\n- Story-writing is blocked because scope has not been bounded at the capability level\n\n# Inputs\n\n- **References** to one or more sections of source material (vision doc, product brief,\n  strategy doc, OKRs, or prior epics)\n- **Output file path**: In Liza mode, assigned by the Orchestrator on the blackboard. In Pairing\n  mode, propose a path under the project's epic directory and confirm with the human before writing.\n\n**Scope discipline (two-tier):**\n- **Upfront:** Read task references and scan existing epics in the same domain for consistency.\n  Same domain = same parent directory, or epics referenced by the same vision doc section.\n  This minimal consistency check is always permitted.\n- **Reviewer-driven:** Broader expansion only when the reviewer's feedback identifies specific\n  additional material to consult.\n\nIn both cases, declare what you read and why in the References section.\n\n# Output Format\n\nProduce a markdown file at the output path.\nUse the [Epic format](references/epic-format.md) template.\n\n# Protocol\n\n## 0. Size\n\nSkim the source material for obvious splitting signals before deep parsing. A badly-sized epic fans\nout into N Story Writer tasks before anyone notices the framing was off.\n\n**Granularity signals:**\n\n| Signal | Diagnosis |\n|--------|-----------|\n| Scope spans multiple independent persona clusters or unrelated subsystems | Too broad — split at capability boundary |\n| Would produce >8 user stories to cover its scope | Too broad — find a natural seam |\n| Completion criteria require outcomes across unrelated subsystems | Too broad — each subsystem likely deserves its own epic |\n| Description contains conjunctions joining unrelated capabilities (\"auth and notifications and reporting\") | Too broad — composite epic smell |\n| Entire scope is a single user action with one acceptance criterion | Too narrow — this is a story, not an epic |\n| Could be implemented in a single coding task without further decomposition | Too narrow — skip the Story Writer stage |\n| Would produce fewer than 2 meaningful user stories | Too narrow — merge with an adjacent epic or promote directly |\n| Cannot be delivered or validated independently of another epic | Too coupled — reconsider the boundary |\n\nIf a single epic's scope spans multiple independent capability areas, flag this — the epic is too\nbroad and needs splitting. This is about epic sizing, not about the number of epics a task produces.\nWhen a planner task decomposes a vision document, producing multiple well-sized epics from one\ntask is normal — apply this skill once per epic boundary.\n\nIf sizing is ambiguous, flag before proceeding. A wrong cut here is more expensive to fix than a\nbrief hold.\n\n## 1. Parse\n\nRead the source material. Before writing anything, identify:\n\n1. **The outcome**: what ships, what changes for the user, how success is measured\n2. **The personas**: who benefits and in what context — if the source doesn't name them, infer the\n   minimum set from the described actions\n3. **The capabilities**: the coarse functional groupings that together constitute the epic\n4. **What is explicitly excluded**: the source material almost always implies adjacent scope; name it\n5. **What is unresolved**: gaps, contradictions, or decisions the source defers\n\nDo not start writing until you can answer all five. If you cannot answer one, it becomes an Open\nQuestion — not a blank you fill with imagination.\n\n## 2. Decompose into Capabilities\n\nA capability is a user-facing behavior the team can build, test, and hand off to a Story Writer as\na bounded unit. It is not a technical module, a sprint, or a story. It is a slice of product\nbehavior.\n\nEach capability must pass the self-containment test defined in the Objective: a Story Writer\nhanded the Personas, General Information, and this capability section can begin writing without\nreading the vision source.\n\n**Capability heuristics:**\n- A capability named after a technical concern (\"database layer\", \"API integration\") is\n  probably not a capability — it's a task. Find the user-facing behavior it enables and name that.\n- Capabilities have a natural partial order: identify true ordering constraints (CAP-B cannot be\n  built without CAP-A's output) vs. merely convenient ones. Do not over-constrain the plan.\n\n**Story document planning:**\nFor each capability, list the story documents it decomposes into. A story document covers one\ncohesive unit of work a Story Writer can own independently. You are naming documents, not writing\nstories — the Story Writer does that. Each entry needs only a short title and any known dependency\nnotes.\n\n## 3. Write\n\n**Completion Criteria** replace vague success metrics. They are the falsifiable condition that\ncloses the epic: when all story ACs pass, the completion criteria must be satisfied. Write them\nas observable outcomes, not directions. \"Users can create, edit, and delete tasks without data\nloss\" is a completion criterion. \"Improve task management\" is not. If you cannot write falsifiable\ncompletion criteria, the epic scope is not yet understood — surface it as an Open Question.\n\n**Personas** at the epic level describe who benefits from the whole epic. Capabilities may\nnarrow to specific sub-personas — note this in the capability description where relevant. A useful\npersona includes environment and skill level when they affect product decisions. Compare:\n\"Operator: a person running the platform\" vs. \"Ops Engineer: a backend engineer on call who\nmonitors the platform via terminal and alerts and needs concise, machine-parseable output.\" The\nsecond persona constrains every capability under it and tells the Story Writer what conventions\nto assume.\n\n**Out of Scope** is not optional. It protects Story Writers from scope absorption and the team from\nscope creep. Name adjacent capabilities the source implies but this epic deliberately excludes.\nIf it's not named, Story Writers will assume it's included.\n\n**Assumptions** at the epic level are strategic: they resolve ambiguity in the vision material\nthat would otherwise leave Story Writers unable to bound their own work. They are NOT technical\ndecisions. An assumption that names a data format, protocol, or library is premature solutioning —\nstate the behavioral constraint only.\n\n**Confidence discipline:**\n- HIGH: The source material strongly implies this; any reasonable reader would agree.\n- MEDIUM: Reasonable inference, but the source is silent or oblique.\n- LOW: You had to guess. This is blocking — a human must resolve it before story-writing begins.\n\n**Open Questions** at the epic level are product-level decisions only: personas, scope boundaries,\ncompletion criteria, or capability ordering. Technical open questions belong in story documents,\nnot here.\n\n## 4. Self-Review\n\nBefore submitting for review, verify:\n- [ ] Completion criteria are falsifiable — all story ACs passing satisfies them\n- [ ] Epic decomposes into 3–8 user stories (use story document count as a proxy)\n- [ ] Every capability traces to a source reference — none invented\n- [ ] Every capability passes the Story Writer self-containment test\n- [ ] Every capability has a clear user-facing description (not technical framing)\n- [ ] Personas include environment or skill-level detail where it affects product behavior\n- [ ] Out of Scope names adjacent capabilities the source implies but this epic excludes\n- [ ] No capability bleeds into story-level detail (data types, API shapes, UI copy)\n- [ ] No assumption prescribes implementation — behavioral constraints only\n- [ ] LOW-confidence assumptions are flagged as blocking\n- [ ] No assumption overlaps with an Open Question — if overlap exists, keep the OQ\n- [ ] Capability ordering constraints are true dependencies, not merely convenient ones\n- [ ] Story document titles are scoped correctly — a Story Writer can own each one independently\n- [ ] Re-read the source material — every source section maps to a capability (no gaps), and nothing was added beyond scope\n- [ ] Sibling ambiguities from the same source gap treated consistently across capabilities\n\nIf self-review reveals issues, fix before submitting.\n\n# Constraints\n\n- **DO** write for the Orchestrator and Story Writers, not for management. Be precise and bounded.\n- **DO** check existing epics in the same domain for consistency — contradictions between epic\n  documents surface late and are expensive.\n- **DO** surface contradictions between source references as an Open Question.\n- **DO NOT** write user stories — epics only. Story content belongs in story documents.\n- **DO NOT** modify existing epic documents unless the task explicitly scopes an update.\n- **DO NOT** name technical solutions in capability descriptions. Name user-facing behavior.\n\n# Anti-Patterns\n\n- **Vision Laundering**: Capabilities named after technical layers (\"Auth Service\", \"Data Pipeline\")\n  instead of user-facing behavior (\"User can authenticate via SSO\", \"Operator can monitor ingestion\").\n- **Giant Epic**: Covers multiple independent persona clusters or unrelated subsystems. Flag to\n  Orchestrator and split. The conjunction smell: \"auth and notifications and reporting\" in a single\n  epic description is a reliable signal.\n- **Dwarf Epic**: A single user action with one acceptance criterion — this is a story, not an epic.\n  If it would produce fewer than 2 meaningful user stories, merge or promote directly.\n- **Storified Epic**: Capabilities written with Given/When/Then or at story granularity.\n  An epic describes what; stories describe done.\n- **Unfalsifiable Completion Criteria**: \"users have a better experience.\" Not falsifiable.\n  Write a condition that is either true or false when story ACs are checked.\n- **Missing Out of Scope**: Adjacent capabilities left unnamed. Story Writers will absorb them.\n- **Assumption Burial**: Strategic assumptions embedded in capability descriptions instead of\n  surfaced in the Assumptions section.\n- **Scope Absorption**: Vision says \"support X.\" You write capabilities for X, Y, and Z.\n- **Premature Solutioning**: Capability descriptions that name an API, framework, data format,\n  or storage engine. State the behavioral need only.\n- **Generic Persona**: \"As a User…\" — a persona at the epic level must orient Story Writers.\n  If \"User\" could be anyone, it tells Story Writers nothing about constraints or expectations.\n- **False Dependencies**: CAP-B depends on CAP-A only because they share a concept, not because\n  CAP-B's implementation requires CAP-A's output. Over-constraining the plan delays delivery.\n- **Opaque Capability**: The Story Writer needs to re-read the vision to understand what to build.\n  Every capability must be self-contained enough that it can be handed to a Story Writer as a\n  complete task brief.\n\n# ID Conventions\n\nAll IDs use structured prefixes:\n\n| Prefix | Meaning | Example |\n|--------|---------|---------|\n| EP-NNN | Epic | EP-003 |\n| CAP-NNN | Capability (scoped to epic) | CAP-001 |\n| C-NNN | External component | C-002 |\n| I-NNN-NNN | Interface (composite: I-{component}-{interface}) | I-002-001 |\n| NFR-000-N | Non-functional requirement | NFR-000-1 |\n| ASM-NNN-N | Assumption (000 = general, NNN = capability) | ASM-000-1 |\n| OQ-NNN-N | Open question | OQ-001-1 |\n\nDo not invent new prefixes. If something doesn't fit these categories, it likely belongs in Context\nor is a sign the epic needs rethinking.\n\n# Altitude Discipline\n\nThe hardest judgment in epic-writing is staying at the right altitude. Use this table as a check:\n\n| Too low (story territory) | Right level (epic territory) | Too high (vision territory) |\n|---------------------------|------------------------------|-----------------------------|\n| AC: \"Given a valid token, when…\" | \"User can authenticate without re-entering credentials\" | \"Improve onboarding\" |\n| \"The endpoint returns 200\" | \"Operator can monitor request health in real time\" | \"Better observability\" |\n| \"Use PostgreSQL for storage\" | \"Tasks persist across sessions\" | \"Reliable data\" |\n| \"Validate email format on blur\" | \"User receives actionable feedback on invalid input\" | \"Good UX\" |\n\nIf a capability description reads like a story, it's too low. Rewrite it as a user-facing behavior.\nIf it reads like a goal in an OKR, it's too high. Narrow it to something a Story Writer can bound.\n\n# Integration\n\n| Skill | Relationship |\n|-------|-------------|\n| **user-story-writing** | Direct downstream consumer. Each capability section is a Story Writer task brief. The Story Writer reads the Personas, General Information, and the capability section — nothing else. Unresolved epic assumptions and Open Questions block story-writing from starting. |\n| **detailed-spec-writing** | Complementary. Epics capture product intent; PRDs capture system requirements. An approved epic can seed a PRD for a capability. |\n| **spec-review** | Downstream. Validates epics against completeness/consistency/testability. |\n\n# Mode-Specific Behavior\n\n**Pairing mode:** All interactive prompts apply. Present the draft epic for human review before\nwriting the file. Human may redirect scope, resolve Open Questions inline, or confirm assumptions.\n\n**Liza mode:** Epic Writer operates autonomously within task scope. When a planner task\ndecomposes a vision document, the planner applies this skill once per epic boundary it identifies.\nProducing multiple epic artifacts from a single vision source is normal pipeline behavior — the\n\"flag for splitting\" guidance in Size applies to individual epics that are too broad, not to the\nplanner's decomposition of a vision into multiple epics.\n\n| Pairing Prompt | Liza Behavior |\n|----------------|---------------|\n| \"Source material spans multiple capability areas — split?\" | Applies to a single epic that's too broad. When decomposing a vision into multiple epics, multiple capability areas across epics is expected — flag only if a single epic spans unrelated areas |\n| \"Epic would produce >8 stories — where to split?\" | Find the natural persona or subsystem seam; flag split rationale in Context |\n| \"Epic would produce <2 stories — merge or promote?\" | Flag to Orchestrator via BLOCKED with merge/promote recommendation |\n| \"This assumption is LOW confidence — resolve?\" | Surface in Assumptions section; blocks story-writing until resolved by human |\n| \"Adjacent epic may conflict — check?\" | Read adjacent document, declare in References, note in Context |\n| \"Cannot identify a clear persona for this epic\" | Surface as Open Question — an epic without a persona cannot produce well-bounded stories |\n| \"Cannot write falsifiable completion criteria\" | Surface as Open Question — scope is not yet understood |\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4affd881-5ee2-42ba-96d1-34f2389069cd","uuid":"95e177f9-5596-4c6f-8e77-f07e1d10e90b","timestamp":"2026-04-12T14:40:22.148Z","isSynthetic":true}
