What problem it solves for which persona.\nKeep it brief — the Orchestrator needs orientation, not a lecture.\n\n## Personas\n- **<Persona name>**: <one-line description of who they are, their environment, and what they care about>\n- ...\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n- <ref-type>: <path or link> — <section/line range if applicable>\n- ...\n\n### Completion Criteria\nThe falsifiable condition that closes this epic. When all story ACs pass, this must be satisfied.\nObservable outcome, not a direction.\n\n<one or two sentences stating the condition — e.g., \"Users can create, edit, and delete tasks\nwithout data loss across sessions. Operators can monitor task volume and error rates in real time.\"\nIf you cannot write this yet, surface it as OQ-000-N.>\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n- NFR-000-1: <requirement> — architectural constraints, performance, security, observability,\n  technology mandates, compatibility requirements, etc.\n- ...\n\n### Related External Components\nSummary of all external components referenced by this epic:\n- Component C-NNN - <component name>: <one-line role in this epic>\n- ...\n\n### Interfaces *(include only when this epic defines component boundaries)*\nSummary of all external interfaces referenced by this epic:\n- I-NNN-NNN - <interface name> (Interface NNN of Component C-NNN): <protocol/contract description>\n- ...\n\n### Out of Scope\nExplicit list of what this epic does NOT cover. Adjacent capabilities the Story Writer must not absorb.\n\n### Assumptions\nItems where the vision material was ambiguous and you made a judgment call.\n- **ASM-000-1**: <what you assumed> — *Why*: <reasoning> — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH | MEDIUM | LOW\n\nLOW confidence assumptions are blocking: the human must resolve them before story-writing begins.\n\n### Open Questions\nQuestions that cannot be resolved by assumption. Must be answered before Story Writers begin work.\n- **OQ-000-1**: <question> — *Impact if unresolved*: <what remains unbounded or contradictory>\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - <capability name>\n\nOne sentence: what this capability delivers and for whom.\n\n### References\n- <ref-type>: <path or link> — <section/line range if applicable>\n- ...\n\n### Description\nTwo to four sentences max. Describe the user-facing behavior — what the persona can do that they\ncould not do before. Do not describe implementation. Do not write stories.\n\n### Story Documents\nThe set of story documents this capability decomposes into. One story document per cohesive unit of\nwork a Story Writer can own.\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| <path — assigned by Orchestrator or agreed with human> | <short title> | P1 / P2 / P3 | <dependency note or blank> |\n| ... | | | |\n\n### Depends on:\n- Capability CAP-NNN - <name>: <why — what from that capability is required here>\n- ...\n\n### Out of Scope\nWhat this capability explicitly excludes. Let me write the two epic documents. Let me design them carefully:\n\n---\n\n**EP-001: Core Authentication Flows**\n\n**Goal**: OHM website users can establish accounts, log in, manage sessions, and reset passwords through admin-mediated token flows.\n\n**Context**: OHM's current authentication model — a single shared login for all musicians — is both a security risk and a GDPR liability. EP-001 replaces it with individual accounts: admins invite musicians via one-time links, musicians activate their accounts through a form, and session-based authentication gates access to the site. Password recovery is also admin-mediated with no email infrastructure required.\n\n\nI'm mapping out the three key actors: admins who manage invites and resets from their browser without touching the command line, musicians who activate accounts through simple forms, and a bootstrapper who sets up the initial admin account during deployment.\n\nNow I'm reviewing the relevant documentation across functional specs, technical specs, routing, and authentication ADRs to understand the full scope of what needs to be built. The completion criteria focus on admins being able to generate and display invite and password-reset links, musicians activating accounts and resetting passwords through a single form, and proper session creation for valid credentials.\n\nI'm also noting the non-functional requirements around security: session cookies need to be HttpOnly, Secure, and SameSite=Strict; passwords must use Argon2id hashing; tokens must be cryptographically generated from 32 random bytes and base64url-encoded; sessions last 7 days with rolling expiration; all state-changing requests need CSRF protection; and the UI must be in French.\n\nThe scope excludes musician record management beyond account creation, account anonymization, phone and address consent handling, admin role management, sheet music access display, email infrastructure, self-service account creation, and the public homepage. I'm also working with the assumption that email serves as the unique identifier for login, and that the invite form requires explicit privacy acknowledgement before submission.\n\nNow I'm looking at the first capability around account invitation and activation—the core flow where an admin invites a musician through a one-time link that leads to account setup and platform access. form and account becomes active | P1 | Core activation flow\n| (assigned by Orchestrator) | Musician sees informative message for expired or used invite link | P2 | Depends on activation story\n\nDepends on: None (first capability in the epic)\n\nOut of Scope:\n- Creating the musician record fields (name, instrument, etc.) — EP-002 (ep-2) scope\n- Phone/address consent implications (what consent enables, admin withdrawal) — EP-004 (ep-4) scope\n- Admin role management and last-admin checks on pending account deletion — EP-002 (this phase)\n\nAssumptions:\n- ASM-001-1: Generating a new invite token marks the previous token as `used` (not deleted). *Why*: The spec says \"doing so invalidates any existing token\"; the data model uses a `used` flag; \"marks as used\" is consistent with the used-flag approach and preserves history. — HIGH\n- ASM-001-2: After completing the invite form, the musician is redirected to their home page (profile or event list). *Why*: The functional spec states \"the musician lands on their home page.\" The exact landing page is not specified; story writers may use the event list or profile page. — MEDIUM\n\nNow moving to the login and session management capability. Active accounts authenticate with email and password through a login form, which creates a server-side session with a signed cookie valid for 7 days rolling. Protected routes require a valid active-account session and redirect unauthenticated requests to login, while logout destroys the session server-side and returns to the login page.\n\nLooking at the acceptance criteria and story breakdown: musicians need to log in with valid credentials, login must reject pending and anonymized accounts, unauthenticated access to protected routes redirects to login, logout destroys the session, and a CLI command allows the first admin account to be bootstrapped when none exists. These stories cover the core authentication flow and initial system setup, with the bootstrap command being independent of the web login stories.\n\nThe account invitation flow produces an active account state that's required before sessions can be created. Session invalidation during anonymization is handled by the anonymization flow in a later phase, but the session system itself needs to support that capability—the trigger comes from the anonymization action, not from this phase.\n\nThe emergency admin recovery CLI is a bootstrapping tool for when the last admin loses access, and while it bypasses normal authentication flows, it's really an operational safeguard rather than part of the core authentication system, so I'll keep it as a lower-priority item in this capability.\n\nNow I'm mapping out the stories for CAP-002. I've got the core login and logout flows at priority 1, plus the initial admin account creation during system setup. The emergency recovery for when an admin can't log in goes in as priority 2. That gives me six stories total.\n\nFor CAP-003, I'm defining the password reset capability where an admin can generate a one-time reset link for a musician's account. The admin accesses the musician's account details, creates a PasswordResetToken, and shares the reset URL. The token has an expiration window built in.\n\nWhen the musician uses the link, they set a new password and the system updates the account's password hash while marking the token as consumed. If someone tries to use an expired or already-used link, they get a clear message explaining what happened. The admin can always generate a fresh reset link if needed, but this feature only works for active accounts.\n\nGenerating story documents...\n\nPassword reset isn't available for accounts that are still pending or have been anonymized. This depends on the login and session management work so musicians can actually use their new passwords. Self-service resets and CLI-based admin recovery are out of scope here.\n\nMoving on to the account privileges and sheet music access feature. The goal is to let admins manage who has admin rights while ensuring at least one admin always exists, and to give all authenticated users access to sheet music through a Google Drive link. Since musicians are switching from shared credentials to individual logins, showing them the sheet music benefit right away is crucial.\n\nI'm defining the key personas involved: admins who grant and revoke roles with clear feedback when blocked by the last-admin rule, musicians who access sheet music through a menu item once the link is configured, and the system operator who sets the sheet music URL as an environment variable during deployment. I'm also noting the relevant functional and technical specifications that cover last-admin protection, role checks, configuration, and routing.\n\nThe completion criteria require that admins can grant and revoke the admin role with proper safeguards—specifically, the system must prevent removing the last active admin and show an informative error message. When the sheet music URL is set, authenticated users see a \"Partitions\" menu item; otherwise it stays hidden. Two non-functional requirements are critical: admin status must be verified fresh from the database on each request rather than cached in the session, and last-admin protection is enforced in the application layer itself, not through database constraints.\n\nThe core invariant protecting the system is that at least one active account must always hold the admin role. Beyond this, the sheet music URL comes from an environment variable at deployment time with no admin interface to change it later. Google Drive handles the actual file hosting and access control—the app just provides the link. Out of scope for this work are musician record management, account anonymization, emergency admin recovery tools, additional role types, sheet music search features, and any admin UI for configuring the URL.\n\nI'm noting two key assumptions about last-admin protection: it applies specifically to three operations—revoking admin access, anonymizing an admin account, and deleting a pending admin account—because the functional spec explicitly lists these. Even though a pending account can't log in, blocking its deletion still preserves the invariant. There are no open questions at this point.\n\nFor the admin role management capability, an admin can grant or revoke the admin role from the musician-management UI, but the system prevents any operation that would eliminate all remaining admins.\n\nThe system re-checks admin status directly from the database on each request rather than relying on session state, so a revoked admin loses access immediately on their next page load. The last-admin protection blocks three specific operations with a clear message if they'd result in zero active admins: revoking the role, anonymizing an admin account, and deleting a pending admin account. I'm realizing this protection spans multiple phases—revoking is in this phase, but anonymizing and deleting pending accounts are defined in later epics, which means I'm setting constraints those phases need to implement.\n\nI should clarify the scope: CAP-001 handles the role grant/revoke operations and the last-admin protection for revocation specifically. The protection checks for anonymization and pending deletion belong to their respective epics, so I'll note that assumption rather than trying to define those implementations here.\n\nI've mapped out four stories covering role grants, revocation, last-admin blocking, and per-request database verification. The role verification story needs a note that it applies across all admin routes. This depends on the login and session management epic being in place first.\n\nNow moving to the sheet music access feature — when the environment variable is configured, authenticated users get a \"Partitions\" menu item that links to Google Drive, otherwise it stays hidden. The access control lives in Google Drive itself, not the app. I've got two stories here: one for showing the menu item when configured, and one for hiding it when the variable isn't set.\n\nThat's borderline for an epic — I need at least a couple of meaningful stories. Let me think about splitting this more granularly. I could add a story specifically about the link working correctly, and another about making sure unauthenticated users can't see it even if the URL is set. That gives me three distinct stories covering the visibility rules and the actual functionality.\n\nNow I'm moving on to write out the epic documents themselves. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_011tJ7WexxvHYmGNjrvTpGuL","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01DEj4CBe7qkQBgVwAqMdqXk","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/home/henry/workspace/ohm-website/.worktrees/ep-1/specs/plans/EP-001.md","content":"# Epic EP-001: Core Authentication Flows\n\nStatus: draft\n\n## Goal\n\nUsers can establish individual accounts, log in with personal credentials, maintain a persistent session, and reset their password through admin-mediated one-time-link flows — with no shared credentials and no system email infrastructure.\n\n## Context\n\nOHM's current model gives all musicians a single shared login that exposes personal data, creating a security risk and a GDPR liability. EP-001 replaces it: admins invite musicians via one-time invite links (generated and displayed in the admin UI, sent manually), musicians activate their accounts through a form, and server-side sessions gate access across the application. Password recovery follows the same admin-mediated pattern. A CLI bootstrap command enables the first admin account to be created before any invite flow is possible.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Works via a desktop browser. Generates invite and reset links, copies them from the admin UI, and sends them manually (e.g. from the association's email address). Non-technical: does not interact with the server directly.\n- **Musician**: An association member. Receives invite or reset links from the admin via email. Activates or recovers their account on a single-page form. Not necessarily technical.\n- **System Bootstrapper**: A technical operator performing first deployment. Runs a CLI command to create the initial admin account before any musician accounts exist. Has SSH access to the server.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow, Password Reset, Last-Admin Protection\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity, InviteToken, PasswordResetToken\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Token Generation, CSRF Protection, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public route group, Authenticated route group\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Server-side sessions decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 Account Model, No system email infrastructure\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can generate invite links and password-reset links for musician accounts, see them displayed in the admin UI for copying, and regenerate them when expired. A musician can activate a pending account and reset a password via a single-page form using the provided link. Login with valid active-account credentials creates a persistent session; logout destroys it. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes redirect to the login page. A system bootstrapper can create the first admin account via CLI without going through the invite flow.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Session cookies must be HttpOnly, Secure, and SameSite=Strict.\n- NFR-000-2: Passwords must be hashed with Argon2id; never stored in plain text and never retrievable.\n- NFR-000-3: Invite and password-reset tokens must be generated from a CSPRNG: 32 random bytes, base64url-encoded.\n- NFR-000-4: Session lifetime is 7 days rolling.\n- NFR-000-5: All state-changing HTTP requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) must be CSRF-protected.\n- NFR-000-6: All UI text, error messages, and labels must be in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\nNone. Authentication is entirely internal; no external identity provider or email service is used.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- **Musician record fields** (name, instrument, birth date, phone, address) — ep-2 scope; account creation UI is initiated there.\n- **Phone/address consent implications** (what consent enables for admin editing, admin consent withdrawal on behalf of musician) — ep-4 scope.\n- **Account anonymization flow** — ep-4 scope. Session invalidation triggered by anonymization is owned there.\n- **Admin role management and last-admin protection** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Sheet music access display** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Self-service account creation** — no self-registration; admin-mediated invite flow only.\n- **System email infrastructure** — no emails sent by the system; links are sent manually by admins.\n- **Public homepage** — ep-4 scope.\n- **GDPR processing restriction flag** — ep-4 scope.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-000-1**: Login uses email as the identifier. *Why*: Email is the unique non-anonymized identifier on the Account entity per the information model. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-2**: The privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox on the invite form is required to submit; the phone/address consent checkbox is optional. *Why*: Privacy notice acknowledgement is a legal compliance requirement; the spec lists both fields without mandating either, but consent cannot be revoked once given on this form, while the privacy notice protects the association legally. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-3**: The bootstrap CLI creates an account in `active` state with the admin role already granted, bypassing the invite flow. *Why*: The configuration spec states this explicitly: \"Creates an account in active state and grants it the admin role.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-4**: Generating a new invite or reset token marks the prior token for that account as `used` (not deleted), consistent with the `used` flag in the data model. *Why*: The functional spec says \"doing so invalidates any existing token\"; the data model uses a `used` boolean field — marking as used preserves audit history. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone. All behavioral details are specified in the source material.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - Account Invitation and Activation\n\nAdmin can invite a new musician to the platform via a one-time link; the musician follows it to complete account setup and gain access.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — InviteToken entity\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Token Generation, Public Routes\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/invitation/{token}` routes\n\n### Description\n\nWhen an admin creates a musician account (account creation UI is ep-2 scope), the system generates an InviteToken and displays the invite URL in the admin UI so the admin can copy and send it manually. The musician follows the link and is presented with a form containing a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form atomically transitions the account from `pending` to `active`, sets the password and consent flag, marks the token used, and logs the musician in. Expired or already-used invite links display an informative message; the admin can generate a replacement from the account detail view at any time.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin sees the invite link for a new musician account | P1 | Token generated at account creation (ep-2 scope); this story covers link display in admin UI |\n| TBD | Admin regenerates an invite link, invalidating the existing one | P1 | Depends on invite link display story |\n| TBD | Musician opens the invite link and sees the account-setup form | P1 | Public route — no session required |\n| TBD | Musician submits the setup form and account transitions to active | P1 | Core activation — atomic transition |\n| TBD | Musician sees an informative message for an expired or already-used invite link | P2 | Account remains pending; admin path to new link is shown |\n\n### Depends on\n\nNone. This is the first capability in the authentication flow; account creation (which triggers token generation) is an ep-2 concern but produces the token that this capability acts on.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Musician record field entry (name, email, instrument, birth date, etc.) — ep-2 scope.\n- Phone/address consent implications after activation (what it enables, how it is withdrawn) — ep-4 scope.\n- Admin role assignment during account creation — EP-002 (this phase).\n- Any email sending — admin copies and sends the link manually.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-001-1**: After the invite form is submitted successfully, the musician is redirected to the authenticated home page (event list or profile). *Why*: The functional spec says \"the musician lands on their home page\" without naming a specific route; the story writer chooses the landing page. — ⚠️ Confidence: MEDIUM\n- **ASM-001-2**: The invite form is a public route — accessible without a session. *Why*: The technical spec's public routes table lists `/invitation/{token}` explicitly. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-001-3**: The admin sees the invite URL in the account detail view (the same view used to manage the musician record). *Why*: The functional spec states the invite URL is \"displayed in the admin UI for the admin to copy and send manually\" and \"The admin can generate a new InviteToken at any time from the account detail view.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-002 - Login, Logout, and Session Management\n\nMusicians and admins can log in with their email and password, maintain a persistent session across requests, and log out, with unauthorized access to protected routes blocked.\n\n### References\n\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public routes (`/connexion`, `/deconnexion`), Authenticated route group, middleware stack\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Session-side sessions rationale\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Account States (only `active` accounts may log in)\n\n### Description\n\nAn `active` account can authenticate by submitting email and password on the login form. On success, a server-side session is created and a signed cookie is set; the session is valid for 7 days rolling. Protected routes verify a valid active-account session on every request; unauthenticated requests redirect to the login page. Logout destroys the session server-side and redirects to the login page. A CLI command (`mise run seed-admin`) lets a technical operator create the first admin account when none exists yet, bypassing the invite flow. A second CLI command (`mise run recover-admin`) provides emergency password recovery when the last admin cannot log in.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Musician logs in with valid email and password | P1 | |\n| TBD | Login is rejected for pending and anonymized accounts with an informative message | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | Unauthenticated access to a protected route redirects to the login page | P1 | Depends on session creation story |\n| TBD | Musician logs out and the session is destroyed | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | System bootstrapper creates the first admin account via CLI | P1 | No dependency on web flow stories; requires an empty admin table |\n| TBD | Technical operator resets admin credentials via emergency recovery CLI | P2 | Independent of web flow; requires SSH access |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability CAP-001 — Account Invitation and Activation: The `active` account state (produced by the invite flow) is the prerequisite for session creation. The bootstrap CLI creates an `active` account directly, bypassing this dependency for the first admin only.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Session invalidation on account anonymization — ep-4 scope (triggered by the anonymization action).\n- Admin role verification on admin-only routes — EP-002 CAP-001 (this phase).\n- Password reset — CAP-003 (this epic).\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-002-1**: The login page is accessible without authentication (no redirect loop). *Why*: The technical spec's public routes table lists `/connexion` explicitly. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-002-2**: The bootstrap CLI refuses to run if an active admin account already exists, to prevent duplication. *Why*: The configuration spec states this explicitly. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-002-3**: The emergency recovery CLI accepts an email and new password, verifies the account is `active`, and updates the password hash without checking the admin role. *Why*: The configuration spec states this explicitly: \"Does not check for admin role — this is intentional.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-003 - Password Reset\n\nAdmin can generate a one-time password-reset link for an active account; the musician follows it to set a new password.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Password Reset section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — PasswordResetToken entity\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Token Generation, Password Hashing, Public Routes\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/reinitialiser-mot-de-passe/{token}` routes\n\n### Description\n\nAn admin navigates to a musician's account detail view and generates a PasswordResetToken. The reset URL is displayed in the admin UI for copying and manual sending. The token expires after 7 days. The musician follows the reset link and submits a new password on a form; the account's password hash is updated atomically and the token is marked used. Expired or already-used reset links display an informative message; the admin can generate a replacement at any time. Password reset is only available for `active` accounts; the operation is blocked for `pending` and `anonymized` accounts.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin generates a password-reset link for an active musician account | P1 | |\n| TBD | Admin regenerates a password-reset link, invalidating the existing one | P1 | Depends on reset link generation story |\n| TBD | Musician follows the reset link and submits a new password | P1 | Public route; no session required |\n| TBD | Musician sees an informative message for an expired or already-used reset link | P2 | Account unaffected; admin path to new link is shown |\n| TBD | Password reset is unavailable for pending and anonymized accounts | P1 | Admin UI does not expose reset link action for these states |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability CAP-002 — Login, Logout, and Session Management: The musician must be able to log in with the new password once the reset is complete. EP-001 replaces it: admins invite musicians via one-time invite links (generated and displayed in the admin UI, sent manually), musicians activate their accounts through a form, and server-side sessions gate access across the application. Password recovery follows the same admin-mediated pattern. A CLI bootstrap command enables the first admin account to be created before any invite flow is possible.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Works via a desktop browser. Generates invite and reset links, copies them from the admin UI, and sends them manually (e.g. from the association's email address). Non-technical: does not interact with the server directly.\n- **Musician**: An association member. Receives invite or reset links from the admin via email. Activates or recovers their account on a single-page form. Not necessarily technical.\n- **System Bootstrapper**: A technical operator performing first deployment. Runs a CLI command to create the initial admin account before any musician accounts exist. Has SSH access to the server.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow, Password Reset, Last-Admin Protection\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity, InviteToken, PasswordResetToken\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Token Generation, CSRF Protection, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public route group, Authenticated route group\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Server-side sessions decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 Account Model, No system email infrastructure\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can generate invite links and password-reset links for musician accounts, see them displayed in the admin UI for copying, and regenerate them when expired. A musician can activate a pending account and reset a password via a single-page form using the provided link. Login with valid active-account credentials creates a persistent session; logout destroys it. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes redirect to the login page. A system bootstrapper can create the first admin account via CLI without going through the invite flow.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Session cookies must be HttpOnly, Secure, and SameSite=Strict.\n- NFR-000-2: Passwords must be hashed with Argon2id; never stored in plain text and never retrievable.\n- NFR-000-3: Invite and password-reset tokens must be generated from a CSPRNG: 32 random bytes, base64url-encoded.\n- NFR-000-4: Session lifetime is 7 days rolling.\n- NFR-000-5: All state-changing HTTP requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) must be CSRF-protected.\n- NFR-000-6: All UI text, error messages, and labels must be in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\nNone. Both capabilities are access-control decisions that sit on top of the session infrastructure built in EP-001.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Uses the admin UI to grant or revoke the admin role on other musician accounts. Expects a clear error message when an operation is blocked by last-admin protection.\n- **Musician**: An authenticated association member. Accesses the association's sheet music via a dedicated menu item when the Google Drive link is configured. Does not manage the link; only uses it.\n- **System Operator**: A technical person deploying the application. Sets the `SHEET_MUSIC_URL` environment variable at deploy time. No UI interaction for this; it is a deploy-time configuration.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Last-Admin Protection, Sheet Music Access sections\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity (Roles, Role invariant), Role section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Role Checks section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Environment Variables (`SHEET_MUSIC_URL`)\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Admin route group (role-admin routes), middleware `RequireAdmin`\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/00-data-model.md` — `roles`, `account_roles` tables\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/005-role-model.md` — Association table decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 In scope: admin role grant/revoke, last-admin protection, sheet music Google Drive link\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can grant the admin role to any active account and revoke it from any account that is not the sole remaining admin. The system rejects — with an informative message — any attempt to revoke the admin role when the target account is the last active admin. When `SHEET_MUSIC_URL` is configured at deploy time, all authenticated users see a \"Partitions\" menu item in the navigation; the item is absent when the variable is unset. Unauthenticated users cannot see the menu item.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Admin role must be re-verified from the database on every request — not from cached session state — so that a revoked admin loses access immediately on their next request.\n- NFR-000-2: The last-admin invariant (\"at least one active account holds the admin role at all times\") is enforced at the application layer. It is not enforced by a database constraint.\n- NFR-000-3: The sheet music URL is a deploy-time environment variable (`SHEET_MUSIC_URL`). No admin UI exists to manage it.\n- NFR-000-4: All UI text and error messages are in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\n- **Component C-001 — Google Drive**: Hosts the sheet music files. The application provides only a hyperlink; file access control is managed entirely at the Google Drive level. The application has no visibility into whether the musician can actually access the files.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- **Creating, editing, or deleting musician records** — ep-2 scope.\n- **Account anonymization** (which removes all roles from the account) — ep-4 scope. The last-admin protection check that applies during anonymization is ep-4's responsibility to implement, guided by the invariant defined here.\n- **Deleting a pending admin account** — ep-2 scope. The last-admin protection check for that operation is ep-2's responsibility to implement, guided by the invariant defined here.\n- **Additional role types beyond `admin`** — V1 defines a single role; the schema supports future roles but no further role-type UI is in scope.\n- **Sheet music file management, hosting, or search** — vision \"Later\" feature.\n- **Admin UI to configure the sheet music URL** — by design; deploy-time configuration only.\n- **Emergency admin recovery CLI** — EP-001 CAP-002 scope.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-000-1**: The last-admin protection invariant applies to three operations: (1) revoking the admin role, (2) anonymizing an admin account, (3) deleting a pending admin account. *Why*: The functional spec enumerates exactly these three operations under \"Last-Admin Protection.\" Only (1) is implemented in this epic; (2) and (3) are implemented in ep-4 and ep-2 respectively, but they must honour the same invariant. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-2**: A pending account can hold the admin role (set by an admin before the account is activated), and last-admin protection blocks its deletion if it is the sole admin. *Why*: The functional spec explicitly lists \"Deleting a pending admin account\" as one of the blocked operations, implying the role can be set on a pending account. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-3**: An admin can grant the admin role to themselves (for use during initial setup before other accounts are created). *Why*: The spec places no restriction on self-grant; the bootstrap CLI creates the first admin account, and subsequent grant/revoke is via the admin UI. — ⚠️ Confidence: MEDIUM\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone. All behavioral details are specified in the source material.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - Admin Role Management and Last-Admin Protection\n\nAdmin can grant or revoke the admin role on any account, with the system blocking any operation that would leave the association without a remaining active admin.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Last-Admin Protection section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity (Roles, Role invariant)\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Role Checks section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/admin/musiciens/{id}/role-admin` routes (POST grant, DELETE revoke), `RequireAdmin` middleware\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/00-data-model.md` — `roles`, `account_roles` tables, application invariant note\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/005-role-model.md`\n\n### Description\n\nFrom the admin musician-management UI, an admin can grant the admin role to an active account or revoke it from an account. Any attempt to revoke the admin role from the sole remaining active admin is rejected with an informative message. This capability defines the invariant that governs last-admin protection; the checks for anonymization and pending-account deletion are implemented in ep-4 and ep-2 respectively but honour the same rule.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin grants the admin role to an active musician account | P1 | |\n| TBD | Admin revokes the admin role from a musician account | P1 | Depends on grant story |\n| TBD | System blocks admin role revocation when the account is the sole remaining active admin | P1 | Depends on revoke story |\n| TBD | Admin role is re-verified from the database on every request to admin routes | P1 | Applies to all admin routes; cross-cutting security requirement |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability EP-001 CAP-002 — Login, Logout, and Session Management: The `RequireAdmin` middleware runs after `RequireActiveAccount`; a valid active-account session is required before the role lookup.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Last-admin protection during account anonymization — ep-4 scope.\n- Last-admin protection during pending account deletion — ep-2 scope.\n- Granting or revoking roles other than `admin` — no additional roles in V1.\n- Any role management UI beyond the grant/revoke actions on the musician detail view.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-001-1**: The admin role check counts only `active` accounts with the `admin` role. The spec says the token gets generated at account creation, which is in episode 2, but displaying that link to the admin happens in episode 1—that's the right boundary. Though I'm noticing the functional spec cuts off mid-sentence about when the invite token is actually generated, so I need to clarify that timing assumption.\n\nThe token generation happens during account creation, which is episode 2's responsibility for the musician record itself. But episode 1 owns the invite link generation logic, display, and the flow for completing the invite. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01LnfUSvboEBp2xkGQSdCZBv","type":"tool_result","content":"75\t## Capability CAP-001 - Account Invitation and Activation\n76\t\n77\tAdmin can invite a new musician to the platform via a one-time link; the musician follows it to complete account setup and gain access.\n78\t\n79\t### References\n80\t\n81\t- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow section\n82\t- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — InviteToken entity\n83\t- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Token Generation, Public Routes\n84\t- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/invitation/{token}` routes\n85\t\n86\t### Description\n87\t\n88\tWhen an admin creates a musician account (account creation UI is ep-2 scope), the system generates an InviteToken and displays the invite URL in the admin UI so the admin can copy and send it manually. The musician follows the link and is presented with a form containing a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form atomically transitions the account from `pending` to `active`, sets the password and consent flag, marks the token used, and logs the musician in. Sheet music is the primary day-to-day value for authenticated musicians — the link that replaces the old shared-credential page must be immediately visible after login. Both capabilities are access-control decisions that sit on top of the session infrastructure built in EP-001.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Uses the admin UI to grant or revoke the admin role on other musician accounts. Expects a clear error message when an operation is blocked by last-admin protection.\n- **Musician**: An authenticated association member. Accesses the association's sheet music via a dedicated menu item when the Google Drive link is configured. Does not manage the link; only uses it.\n- **System Operator**: A technical person deploying the application. Sets the `SHEET_MUSIC_URL` environment variable at deploy time. No UI interaction for this; it is a deploy-time configuration.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Last-Admin Protection, Sheet Music Access sections\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity (Roles, Role invariant), Role section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Role Checks section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Environment Variables (`SHEET_MUSIC_URL`)\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Admin route group (role-admin routes), middleware `RequireAdmin`\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/00-data-model.md` — `roles`, `account_roles` tables\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/005-role-model.md` — Association table decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 In scope: admin role grant/revoke, last-admin protection, sheet music Google Drive link\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can grant the admin role to any active account and revoke it from any account that is not the sole remaining admin. The system rejects — with an informative message — any attempt to revoke the admin role when the target account is the last active admin. When `SHEET_MUSIC_URL` is configured at deploy time, all authenticated users see a \"Partitions\" menu item in the navigation; the item is absent when the variable is unset. Unauthenticated users cannot see the menu item.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Admin role must be re-verified from the database on every request — not from cached session state — so that a revoked admin loses access immediately on their next request.\n- NFR-000-2: The last-admin invariant (\"at least one active account holds the admin role at all times\") is enforced at the application layer. It is not enforced by a database constraint.\n- NFR-000-3: The sheet music URL is a deploy-time environment variable (`SHEET_MUSIC_URL`). No admin UI exists to manage it.\n- NFR-000-4: All UI text and error messages are in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\n- **Component C-001 — Google Drive**: Hosts the sheet music files. The application provides only a hyperlink; file access control is managed entirely at the Google Drive level. The application has no visibility into whether the musician can actually access the files.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- **Creating, editing, or deleting musician records** — ep-2 scope.\n- **Account anonymization** (which removes all roles from the account) — ep-4 scope. The last-admin protection check that applies during anonymization is ep-4's responsibility to implement, guided by the invariant defined here.\n- **Deleting a pending admin account** — ep-2 scope. The last-admin protection check for that operation is ep-2's responsibility to implement, guided by the invariant defined here.\n- **Additional role types beyond `admin`** — V1 defines a single role; the schema supports future roles but no further role-type UI is in scope.\n- **Sheet music file management, hosting, or search** — vision \"Later\" feature.\n- **Admin UI to configure the sheet music URL** — by design; deploy-time configuration only.\n- **Emergency admin recovery CLI** — EP-001 CAP-002 scope.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-000-1**: The last-admin protection invariant applies to three operations: (1) revoking the admin role, (2) anonymizing an admin account, (3) deleting a pending admin account. *Why*: The functional spec enumerates exactly these three operations under \"Last-Admin Protection.\" Only (1) is implemented in this epic; (2) and (3) are implemented in ep-4 and ep-2 respectively, but they must honour the same invariant. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-2**: A pending account can hold the admin role (set by an admin before the account is activated), and last-admin protection blocks its deletion if it is the sole admin. *Why*: The functional spec explicitly lists \"Deleting a pending admin account\" as one of the blocked operations, implying the role can be set on a pending account. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-3**: An admin can grant the admin role to themselves (for use during initial setup before other accounts are created). *Why*: The spec places no restriction on self-grant; the bootstrap CLI creates the first admin account, and subsequent grant/revoke is via the admin UI. — ⚠️ Confidence: MEDIUM\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone. All behavioral details are specified in the source material.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - Admin Role Management and Last-Admin Protection\n\nAdmin can grant or revoke the admin role on any account, with the system blocking any operation that would leave the association without a remaining active admin.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Last-Admin Protection section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity (Roles, Role invariant)\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Role Checks section\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/admin/musiciens/{id}/role-admin` routes (POST grant, DELETE revoke), `RequireAdmin` middleware\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/00-data-model.md` — `roles`, `account_roles` tables, application invariant note\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/005-role-model.md`\n\n### Description\n\nFrom the admin musician-management UI, an admin can grant the admin role to an active account or revoke it from an account. EP-001 replaces it: admins invite musicians via one-time invite links (generated and displayed in the admin UI, sent manually), musicians activate their accounts through a form, and server-side sessions gate access across the application. Password recovery follows the same admin-mediated pattern. A CLI bootstrap command enables the first admin account to be created before any invite flow is possible.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Works via a desktop browser. Generates invite and reset links, copies them from the admin UI, and sends them manually (e.g. from the association's email address). Non-technical: does not interact with the server directly.\n- **Musician**: An association member. Receives invite or reset links from the admin via email. Activates or recovers their account on a single-page form. Not necessarily technical.\n- **System Bootstrapper**: A technical operator performing first deployment. Runs a CLI command to create the initial admin account before any musician accounts exist. Has SSH access to the server.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow, Password Reset, Last-Admin Protection\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity, InviteToken, PasswordResetToken\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Token Generation, CSRF Protection, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public route group, Authenticated route group\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Server-side sessions decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 Account Model, No system email infrastructure\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can generate invite links and password-reset links for musician accounts, see them displayed in the admin UI for copying, and regenerate them when expired. A musician can activate a pending account and reset a password via a single-page form using the provided link. Login with valid active-account credentials creates a persistent session; logout destroys it. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes redirect to the login page. A system bootstrapper can create the first admin account via CLI without going through the invite flow.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Session cookies must be HttpOnly, Secure, and SameSite=Strict.\n- NFR-000-2: Passwords must be hashed with Argon2id; never stored in plain text and never retrievable.\n- NFR-000-3: Invite and password-reset tokens must be generated from a CSPRNG: 32 random bytes, base64url-encoded.\n- NFR-000-4: Session lifetime is 7 days rolling.\n- NFR-000-5: All state-changing HTTP requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) must be CSRF-protected.\n- NFR-000-6: All UI text, error messages, and labels must be in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\nNone. Authentication is entirely internal; no external identity provider or email service is used.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- **Musician record fields** (name, instrument, birth date, phone, address) — ep-2 scope; account creation UI is initiated there.\n- **Phone/address consent implications** (what consent enables for admin editing, admin consent withdrawal on behalf of musician) — ep-4 scope.\n- **Account anonymization flow** — ep-4 scope. Session invalidation triggered by anonymization is owned there.\n- **Admin role management and last-admin protection** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Sheet music access display** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Self-service account creation** — no self-registration; admin-mediated invite flow only.\n- **System email infrastructure** — no emails sent by the system; links are sent manually by admins.\n- **Public homepage** — ep-4 scope.\n- **GDPR processing restriction flag** — ep-4 scope.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-000-1**: Login uses email as the identifier. *Why*: Email is the unique non-anonymized identifier on the Account entity per the information model. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-2**: The privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox on the invite form is required to submit; the phone/address consent checkbox is optional. *Why*: Privacy notice acknowledgement is a legal compliance requirement; the spec lists both fields without mandating either, but consent cannot be revoked once given on this form, while the privacy notice protects the association legally. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-3**: The bootstrap CLI creates an account in `active` state with the admin role already granted, bypassing the invite flow. *Why*: The configuration spec states this explicitly: \"Creates an account in active state and grants it the admin role.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-4**: Generating a new invite or reset token marks the prior token for that account as `used` (not deleted), consistent with the `used` flag in the data model. *Why*: The functional spec says \"doing so invalidates any existing token\"; the data model uses a `used` boolean field — marking as used preserves audit history. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone. All behavioral details are specified in the source material.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - Account Invitation and Activation\n\nAdmin can invite a new musician to the platform via a one-time link; the musician follows it to complete account setup and gain access.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — InviteToken entity\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Token Generation, Public Routes\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/invitation/{token}` routes\n\n### Description\n\nWhen an admin creates a musician account (account creation UI is ep-2 scope), the system generates an InviteToken and displays the invite URL in the admin UI so the admin can copy and send it manually. The musician follows the link and is presented with a form containing a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form atomically transitions the account from `pending` to `active`, sets the password and consent flag, marks the token used, and logs the musician in. Expired or already-used invite links display an informative message; the admin can generate a replacement from the account detail view at any time.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin sees the invite link for a new musician account | P1 | Token generated at account creation (ep-2 scope); this story covers link display in admin UI |\n| TBD | Admin regenerates an invite link, invalidating the existing one | P1 | Depends on invite link display story |\n| TBD | Musician opens the invite link and sees the account-setup form | P1 | Public route — no session required |\n| TBD | Musician submits the setup form and account transitions to active | P1 | Core activation — atomic transition |\n| TBD | Musician sees an informative message for an expired or already-used invite link | P2 | Account remains pending; admin path to new link is shown |\n\n### Depends on\n\nNone. This is the first capability in the authentication flow; account creation (which triggers token generation) is an ep-2 concern but produces the token that this capability acts on.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Musician record field entry (name, email, instrument, birth date, etc.) — ep-2 scope.\n- Phone/address consent implications after activation (what it enables, how it is withdrawn) — ep-4 scope.\n- Admin role assignment during account creation — EP-002 (this phase).\n- Any email sending — admin copies and sends the link manually.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-001-1**: After the invite form is submitted successfully, the musician is redirected to the authenticated home page (event list or profile). *Why*: The functional spec says \"the musician lands on their home page\" without naming a specific route; the story writer chooses the landing page. — ⚠️ Confidence: MEDIUM\n- **ASM-001-2**: The invite form is a public route — accessible without a session. *Why*: The technical spec's public routes table lists `/invitation/{token}` explicitly. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-001-3**: The admin sees the invite URL in the account detail view (the same view used to manage the musician record). *Why*: The functional spec states the invite URL is \"displayed in the admin UI for the admin to copy and send manually\" and \"The admin can generate a new InviteToken at any time from the account detail view.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-002 - Login, Logout, and Session Management\n\nMusicians and admins can log in with their email and password, maintain a persistent session across requests, and log out, with unauthorized access to protected routes blocked.\n\n### References\n\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public routes (`/connexion`, `/deconnexion`), Authenticated route group, middleware stack\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Session-side sessions rationale\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Account States (only `active` accounts may log in)\n\n### Description\n\nAn `active` account can authenticate by submitting email and password on the login form. On success, a server-side session is created and a signed cookie is set; the session is valid for 7 days rolling. Protected routes verify a valid active-account session on every request; unauthenticated requests redirect to the login page. Logout destroys the session server-side and redirects to the login page. A CLI command (`mise run seed-admin`) lets a technical operator create the first admin account when none exists yet, bypassing the invite flow. A second CLI command (`mise run recover-admin`) provides emergency password recovery when the last admin cannot log in.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Musician logs in with valid email and password | P1 | |\n| TBD | Login is rejected for pending and anonymized accounts with an informative message | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | Unauthenticated access to a protected route redirects to the login page | P1 | Depends on session creation story |\n| TBD | Musician logs out and the session is destroyed | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | System bootstrapper creates the first admin account via CLI | P1 | No dependency on web flow stories; requires an empty admin table |\n| TBD | Technical operator resets admin credentials via emergency recovery CLI | P2 | Independent of web flow; requires SSH access |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability CAP-001 — Account Invitation and Activation: The `active` account state (produced by the invite flow) is the prerequisite for session creation. The reset URL is displayed in the admin UI for copying and manual sending. The token expires after 7 days. The musician follows the reset link and submits a new password on a form; the account's password hash is updated atomically and the token is marked used. Expired or already-used reset links display an informative message; the admin can generate a replacement at any time. Password reset is only available for `active` accounts; the operation is blocked for `pending` and `anonymized` accounts.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin generates a password-reset link for an active musician account | P1 | |\n| TBD | Admin regenerates a password-reset link, invalidating the existing one | P1 | Depends on reset link generation story |\n| TBD | Musician follows the reset link and submits a new password | P1 | Public route; no session required |\n| TBD | Musician sees an informative message for an expired or already-used reset link | P2 | Account unaffected; admin path to new link is shown |\n| TBD | Password reset is unavailable for pending and anonymized accounts | P1 | Admin UI does not expose reset link action for these states |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability CAP-002 — Login, Logout, and Session Management: The musician must be able to log in with the new password once the reset is complete. The bootstrap CLI creates an `active` admin account directly without going through the invite flow; all login and session stories can be built and tested independently. CAP-001 (invite flow) depends on this capability — not the reverse.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Session invalidation on account anonymization","originalFile":"# Epic EP-001: Core Authentication Flows\n\nStatus: draft\n\n## Goal\n\nUsers can establish individual accounts, log in with personal credentials, maintain a persistent session, and reset their password through admin-mediated one-time-link flows — with no shared credentials and no system email infrastructure.\n\n## Context\n\nOHM's current model gives all musicians a single shared login that exposes personal data, creating a security risk and a GDPR liability. EP-001 replaces it: admins invite musicians via one-time invite links (generated and displayed in the admin UI, sent manually), musicians activate their accounts through a form, and server-side sessions gate access across the application. Password recovery follows the same admin-mediated pattern. A CLI bootstrap command enables the first admin account to be created before any invite flow is possible.\n\n## Personas\n\n- **Admin**: An association member with management privileges. Works via a desktop browser. Generates invite and reset links, copies them from the admin UI, and sends them manually (e.g. from the association's email address). Non-technical: does not interact with the server directly.\n- **Musician**: An association member. Receives invite or reset links from the admin via email. Activates or recovers their account on a single-page form. Not necessarily technical.\n- **System Bootstrapper**: A technical operator performing first deployment. Runs a CLI command to create the initial admin account before any musician accounts exist. Has SSH access to the server.\n\n## General information\n\nApplies to: the entire epic scope.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow, Password Reset, Last-Admin Protection\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — Account entity, InviteToken, PasswordResetToken\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Token Generation, CSRF Protection, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public route group, Authenticated route group\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Server-side sessions decision\n- Goal spec: `specs/goals/vision.md` — V1 Account Model, No system email infrastructure\n\n### Completion Criteria\n\nAn admin can generate invite links and password-reset links for musician accounts, see them displayed in the admin UI for copying, and regenerate them when expired. A musician can activate a pending account and reset a password via a single-page form using the provided link. Login with valid active-account credentials creates a persistent session; logout destroys it. Unauthenticated requests to protected routes redirect to the login page. A system bootstrapper can create the first admin account via CLI without going through the invite flow.\n\n### Non-Functional Requirements\n\n- NFR-000-1: Session cookies must be HttpOnly, Secure, and SameSite=Strict.\n- NFR-000-2: Passwords must be hashed with Argon2id; never stored in plain text and never retrievable.\n- NFR-000-3: Invite and password-reset tokens must be generated from a CSPRNG: 32 random bytes, base64url-encoded.\n- NFR-000-4: Session lifetime is 7 days rolling.\n- NFR-000-5: All state-changing HTTP requests (POST, PUT, PATCH, DELETE) must be CSRF-protected.\n- NFR-000-6: All UI text, error messages, and labels must be in French.\n\n### Related External Components\n\nNone. Authentication is entirely internal; no external identity provider or email service is used.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- **Musician record fields** (name, instrument, birth date, phone, address) — ep-2 scope; account creation UI is initiated there.\n- **Phone/address consent implications** (what consent enables for admin editing, admin consent withdrawal on behalf of musician) — ep-4 scope.\n- **Account anonymization flow** — ep-4 scope. Session invalidation triggered by anonymization is owned there.\n- **Admin role management and last-admin protection** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Sheet music access display** — EP-002 (this phase).\n- **Self-service account creation** — no self-registration; admin-mediated invite flow only.\n- **System email infrastructure** — no emails sent by the system; links are sent manually by admins.\n- **Public homepage** — ep-4 scope.\n- **GDPR processing restriction flag** — ep-4 scope.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-000-1**: Login uses email as the identifier. *Why*: Email is the unique non-anonymized identifier on the Account entity per the information model. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-2**: The privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox on the invite form is required to submit; the phone/address consent checkbox is optional. *Why*: Privacy notice acknowledgement is a legal compliance requirement; the spec lists both fields without mandating either, but consent cannot be revoked once given on this form, while the privacy notice protects the association legally. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-3**: The bootstrap CLI creates an account in `active` state with the admin role already granted, bypassing the invite flow. *Why*: The configuration spec states this explicitly: \"Creates an account in active state and grants it the admin role.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-000-4**: Generating a new invite or reset token marks the prior token for that account as `used` (not deleted), consistent with the `used` flag in the data model. *Why*: The functional spec says \"doing so invalidates any existing token\"; the data model uses a `used` boolean field — marking as used preserves audit history. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone. All behavioral details are specified in the source material.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-001 - Account Invitation and Activation\n\nAdmin can invite a new musician to the platform via a one-time link; the musician follows it to complete account setup and gain access.\n\n### References\n\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Invite Flow section\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/00-information-model.md` — InviteToken entity\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Token Generation, Public Routes\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — `/invitation/{token}` routes\n\n### Open Questions\n\n- **OQ-001-1**: The auth-security spec (`specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md`, Public Routes table) lists the invite route as `/invite/:token`, while the routing spec (`specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md`) lists it as `/invitation/{token}`. These are inconsistent. — *Impact if unresolved*: Story Writers will encounter two different paths and cannot determine the canonical route without consulting additional material. The routing spec is the authoritative source for path definitions and should be treated as correct; the auth-security spec's Public Routes table contains a stale path and should be updated in a separate task.\n\n### Description\n\nWhen an admin creates a musician account (account creation UI is ep-2 scope), the system generates an InviteToken and displays the invite URL in the admin UI so the admin can copy and send it manually. The musician follows the link and is presented with a form containing a password field, a privacy notice acknowledgement checkbox, and a phone/address consent checkbox. Submitting the form atomically transitions the account from `pending` to `active`, sets the password and consent flag, marks the token used, and logs the musician in. Expired or already-used invite links display an informative message; the admin can generate a replacement from the account detail view at any time.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Admin sees the invite link for a new musician account | P1 | Token generated at account creation (ep-2 scope); this story covers link display in admin UI |\n| TBD | Admin regenerates an invite link, invalidating the existing one | P1 | Depends on invite link display story |\n| TBD | Musician opens the invite link and sees the account-setup form | P1 | Public route — no session required |\n| TBD | Musician submits the setup form and account transitions to active | P1 | Core activation — atomic transition |\n| TBD | Musician sees an informative message for an expired or already-used invite link | P2 | Account remains pending; admin path to new link is shown |\n\n### Depends on\n\nNone. This is the first capability in the authentication flow; account creation (which triggers token generation) is an ep-2 concern but produces the token that this capability acts on.\n\n### Out of Scope\n\n- Musician record field entry (name, email, instrument, birth date, etc.) — ep-2 scope.\n- Phone/address consent implications after activation (what it enables, how it is withdrawn) — ep-4 scope.\n- Admin role assignment during account creation — EP-002 (this phase).\n- Any email sending — admin copies and sends the link manually.\n\n### Assumptions\n\n- **ASM-001-1**: After the invite form is submitted successfully, the musician is redirected to the authenticated home page (event list or profile). *Why*: The functional spec says \"the musician lands on their home page\" without naming a specific route; the story writer chooses the landing page. — ⚠️ Confidence: MEDIUM\n- **ASM-001-2**: The invite form is a public route — accessible without a session. *Why*: The technical spec's public routes table lists `/invitation/{token}` explicitly. — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n- **ASM-001-3**: The admin sees the invite URL in the account detail view (the same view used to manage the musician record). *Why*: The functional spec states the invite URL is \"displayed in the admin UI for the admin to copy and send manually\" and \"The admin can generate a new InviteToken at any time from the account detail view.\" — ⚠️ Confidence: HIGH\n\n### Open Questions\n\nNone.\n\n---\n\n## Capability CAP-002 - Login, Logout, and Session Management\n\nMusicians and admins can log in with their email and password, maintain a persistent session across requests, and log out, with unauthorized access to protected routes blocked.\n\n### References\n\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/01-auth-and-security.md` — Session-Based Authentication, Password Hashing, Public Routes, Role Checks\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/02-configuration.md` — Bootstrap: First Admin Account, Emergency Admin Recovery\n- Technical spec: `specs/technical-specs/04-routing.md` — Public routes (`/connexion`, `/deconnexion`), Authenticated route group, middleware stack\n- Technical ADR: `specs/technical-adrs/001-authentication.md` — Session-side sessions rationale\n- Functional spec: `specs/functional-specs/01-account-lifecycle.md` — Account States (only `active` accounts may log in)\n\n### Description\n\nAn `active` account can authenticate by submitting email and password on the login form. On success, a server-side session is created and a signed cookie is set; the session is valid for 7 days rolling. Protected routes verify a valid active-account session on every request; unauthenticated requests redirect to the login page. Logout destroys the session server-side and redirects to the login page. A CLI command (`mise run seed-admin`) lets a technical operator create the first admin account when none exists yet, bypassing the invite flow. A second CLI command (`mise run recover-admin`) provides emergency password recovery when the last admin cannot log in.\n\n### Story Documents\n\n| Story Doc | Title | Priority | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|----------|-------|\n| TBD | Musician logs in with valid email and password | P1 | |\n| TBD | Login is rejected for pending and anonymized accounts with an informative message | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | Unauthenticated access to a protected route redirects to the login page | P1 | Depends on session creation story |\n| TBD | Musician logs out and the session is destroyed | P1 | Depends on login story |\n| TBD | System bootstrapper creates the first admin account via CLI | P1 | No dependency on web flow stories; requires an empty admin table |\n| TBD | Technical operator resets admin credentials via emergency recovery CLI | P2 | Independent of web flow; requires SSH access |\n\n### Depends on\n\n- Capability CAP-001 — Account Invitation and Activation: The `active` account state (produced by the invite flow) is the prerequisite for session creation.
